croſſe ouer cup incontinent full wine tooke cuppe duke great maruaile thereof aſſoone cuppe handes voyd againe quoth duke thou haſt enchaunted mee sir quoth huon none enchaunter ſin ſet worthy hold borne euill houre art thou ſo hardy quoth duke ſpeake thus vnto repute thee proud foole thou knoweſt well lyeth power deſtroy thée man dare ſay contrarie yet pray thée tell thy name thou wert borne whether thou goeſt kinne thou art sir quoth huon thinge may fal vnto wil hide name kindred therefore sir know troth borne bourdeaux vpon gerone sonne duke seuin dead ſeauen yeares paſſed duke heard huon nephew ſaide sonne brother nephew haſt thou taken citie lodging mine ſhewe mée whether thou wilt goe sir quoth huon going babilon admirall gaudiſe doe meſſuage king charlemaine fraunce bycauſe ſlewe sonne ſo ſhewed vncle aduenture king taken away land ſhould haue againe vntill done meſſuage admirall faire nephew quoth duke like wiſe baniſhed realme fraunce ſince haue denyed faith ieſus chriſt ſince married héere countrey great ladie whome haue great land gouerne whereof lord nephew ſhall goe lodge caſtle morrow ſhall haue baron conduct vntill come vnto babilon sir quoth huon thanke ſince pleaſure goe pallaice gerames priuily ſayd vnto sir goe thether may perhaps repent ſelfe ſo may well quoth gonder prouoſt huon commanded truſſe vp geare make readie horſes tooke cup left ſtill horne prouoſt thus huon went vncle vnto caſtle lay night next morning huon came vnto vncle take leaue faire nephew quoth duke require tarie vntill baron come ſhall conduct iourney sir quoth huon ſéeing pleaſeth content abide ſo ſat downe dinner chap xxviii ¶ duke thought haue murdered huon owne nephew while ſat table traytour duke ſawe nephewe ſit table hee called knight borne fraunce called geffrey came fraunce duke like manner denyed law chriſt ſecret duke duke priuily ſayde vnto fréend go arme hundred six ſcore paynim cauſe come hether let ſlay nephew come one eſcape ſhall looſe fauour sir quoth geffrey ſhalbe done geffrey went chamber whereas two hundred armour hanging came thether ſaid within himſelfe ala good lord villaine traytour would ſlay sonne brother fraunce great courteſie béene dead ſlaine duke seuin father ſuccoured reaſon mée render againe ſome reward vnto sonne god confound mee hath ill ſhall rather cauſe falſe duke buy dearely treaſon would doe vnto nephewe ſame ſeaſon caſtle seauenſcore priſoners frenchman taken vpon sea duke kept priſon intent put death ſo cruell againſt chriſtian men god neuer forgetteth ſeruants ſucoured geffrey went priſon ſaid priſoners sir ſaue liues come follow priſoners incontinent yſſued priſon followed geffrey brought chamber whereas harneſſe hanged cauſed armed ſaid sir haue courage iſſue hence time ſhew vertue sir quoth dye quarrell ſhall doe commaundement come bondage fréedome geffrey hearde right ioyfull ſayd sir know ſurely héere pallaice dinner ye son duke seuin bourdeaux nephewe duke lord houſe chriſtened hath denyed faith lord god hath commaunded cauſe seauenſcore paynim armed come ſlay nephewe company thus armed sword ſides followed geffrey pallaice entred huon ſayd duke vncle sir theſe men harneſſe enter hall ſuch ye haue commaunded come hether conduct iourney huon quoth duke otherwiſe thou thinkeſt thinke ſurely die remedie thou ſhalt neuer ſée faire day ſaid sir ſtep forth looke chriſtian man eſcape let ſlaine chap xxix ¶how ayd geffrey priſoners huon ſuccoured ſlew paynim duke fled beſieged caſtle huon ſawe malice vncle falſe treaſon ſore abaſhed aroſe vp ſuddainly put helmet head tooke sword hand geffrey came cryed saint denis noble frenchman take héede paynim eſcape aliue ſlay ſorrow frenchman drew sword fought paynim part ſo within ſhort time ſlaine duke ſawe howe paynim ſlewe men hée great feare life ſo fled away ſecret chamber huon perceiued frenchman thus ſuccoured purſued duke sword hand bloudy bloud paynim ſlaine trayterous duke ſaw nephewe ſo followed hee fledde chamber chamber vntill hee came windowe opening vppon garden ſide ſo leapt thereat ran away whereof huon geffrey frenchman right ſorrowfull cloſed gate lifted vp bridge entent ſhould taken within came hall whereas one tooke acquaintance another whereof great ioy god ſuccoured ioy béen turned ſorrow duke eſcaped came ye towne made crye many able beare armour ſhould come vnto ſo could make came pallaice tenne thouſand perſons ſware death chriſtian men within pallaice duke ſaw hée ſuch number ioyfull commanded engins raiſed vp ladder euerie part pike mattockes brake downe corner tower chriſtian men within defended ſelues valiantly defence little auailed lord god mightily ſuccoured huon knewe danger hée ſore diſpleaſed ſayd ah good lord ought ſore agréeued ſee wée thus kept mine vncle feare ſhall neuer ſée dayes gerames ſaid sir loue god blowe nowe horne ala quoth huon power doe prouoſt gonder hath kéeping ah huon quoth gerames ill houre acquainted nowe folly pride way diſtruction thus deuiſing gonder prouoſt came duke ſaid sir haue great maruaile thus deſtroy owne pallaice great folly doe therein rather would councell leaue aſſault let peace made betwéene nephew vpon condition let company go ſafely away prouoſt quoth duke pray 〈◊〉 goe doe beſt thou canſt thou doeſt counſaile prouoſt came pallaice ſayd huon sir god ſake ſpeake mée art thou quoth huon hoſt prouoſt require much loue liues kéepe well pallaice sir quoth huon good counſaile thanke deſire loue beare would help ſaue life deliuer againe horne iuorie tooke kéepe without cannot eſcape death sir quoth prouoſt farre ſo tooke boſome deliuered vnto huon windowe vpon garden ſide chap xxx ¶how king oberon came ſuccoured huon ſlewe paynim except ſuch would chriſtened huon ſlewe duke vncle huon ſaw poſſeſſed horne iuorie hee ioyfull maruaile ſuertie life hée ſet mouth began blowe gerames ſaid ah sir ſhould neuer bee ſo lighte diſcouer ſecrets prouoſt béene vntrue might haue diſcouered ſecrets duke whereby béene loſt dead therefore neuer diſcouer ſecrets alſo sir require yet blowe horne bee yet hurt king oberon commaunded ſo departing quoth huon tarrye vntill ſlaine ſurely blowe without longer tarying ſo blewe ſo ſore bloud came mouth ſo pallaice began ſinge daunce duke al ſuch ſéege pallaice could reſt fell ſinge daunce kinge oberon citie momur ſaide high ah heare fréend huons horne blowe whereby knowe well hath ſome buſineſſe hand wherefore wiſhe ſelfe horne blowne hundred thouſand men well armed made ſooner wiſh citie tormont whereas men ſlewe downe paynim maruaile ſée bloud run downe stréetes like riuer king oberon made cryed many would receiue baptiſme liues ſhould ſaued ſo thereby many chriſtened king oberon came pallaice huon ſawe hee went thanked ſuccour time néede fréend quoth oberon longe beléeue doe commaundements ſhall neuer fayle ſuccour affaire thus towne would beléeue god ſlaine duke taken brought pallaice vnto huon ſawe vncle taken ioyfull duke ſayd faire nephewe require haue pitie ah vntrue traytour quoth huon thou ſhalt neuer depart hence aliue ſhall neuer reſpite thy death ſword ſtrooke vncles head made bodie hanged ouer ye wals towne ilneſſe might alwayes memorie example thus countrey deliuered traytour chap xxxi ¶how king oberon forbad huon ſhould goe towre giant huon would accord went thether whereby great danger death damſell found owne coſen borne fraunce yee haue heard howe king oberon came ſuccoured huon done ſaid vnto huon deare fréend take leaue thée ſhall neuer ſée thée vntill thou haſt ſuffered much paine ill pouerty diſeaſe hard declare thine owne folly huon heard affrayd ſaid sir mee thinkes ſaye great wronge thing power obſerue commaundement fréend quoth oberon ſéeing thou wilt doe ſo remember thy promiſe charge thée vpon paine thy life looſing euer loue thou ſo hardy take way tower dunother maruaylous great tower ſtanding seaſide iulius caeſar cauſed made therein longe time nouriſhed thou neuer ſaweſt ſo faire tower better garniſhed chamber glaſſe windowes within hanged rich tapeſtrie entrie gate two men braſſe holding handes • layle yron wherewith without ceaſe day night beat ſuch meaſure one ſtriketh • tooke vpon aduenture might heard though neuer ſo perilous would neuer eſchew feare death therefore sir ha • rather die forſake fight yt gyant n • man ſhall let sir promiſe ere returne againe conquer hoſt ſo companie departed ſo road ouer hils dal night day certaine ſpace without finding aduenture worthy memorie laſt came néere seaſide whereas tower gyaunt huon ſaw ſayd vnto companie sir yonder find aduentures therefore ſpeake contrarie ere ſléepe fight gyant though harder yron yet ſhall ſlay mée gerames abyde héere meadowe vntill returne againe sir quoth gerames wéeping ſore diſpleaſeth bee better therefore recommende vnto ſauegard god thus huon departed left companie heauily complayning huon armed himſelfe ſo tooke way kiſſed men one another tooke horne cup ſo alone foot went foorth reſted vntill came gate caſtle dunother ſaw twoo men braſſe without ceaſing beate • layles beheld well thought manner impoſſible enter without death began conſider hereon himſelfe king oberon ſhewed troth thought without aide grace god impoſſible enter whereuppon beheld place enter laſt ſaw neere piller marble baſon gould faſt tyed chaine approached neere thereto drew ſword wherwith ſtrake thrée great ſtroaks baſon ſo ſound thereof might well heard caſtle within tower damſell called sibilla ſhe heard baſon ſound ſhe great maruaile thereat ſhe went window looked ſaw huon would enter whereuppon ſhe went backe againe ſaid ah good lord knight yonder without would enter gyant awake anone ſlaine thowſand knight together ſhould ſoone deſtroyed ſurely haue great deſire know borne ſéemeth ſhould ſhe returned againe quickly gate opened wicket yſſued ſuch wind cauſed two men flayles ſtand ſtill reſt ſhée opened wicket haſtily ſhée returned chamber huon ſawe little wicket open aduaunced himſelfe entred two men flayles reſt hée went thinking finde opened wicket hée ſore abaſhed could finde creature ſo many chamber wiſt whether goe finde ſought thus ſearched laſt hée ſawe pillar fourtéene men returned caſtle hearkened went ſearching carefully heard voice damſell pitiouſly wéeping came ſhe humbly ſaluted ſaid faire damſell cannot tell vnderſtand language knowe would wherefore make great ſorrowe sir quoth ſhe wéepe becauſe haue great pitie gyant heare within yet ſléepe hap awake dead loſt faire ladie quoth huon pray ſhew borne sir quoth ſhée daughter guinemer time earle saint omers néece duke seuin bourdeaux huon heard right humbly kiſſed ſaide madame knowe troth néere kinſewoman sonne duke seuin pray ſhew aduenture hath brought caſtle sir quoth ſhe father deuotion ſée holy sepulchre loued ſo well would leaue behind sea néere citie eſcalone surry aroſe great tempeſt vpon sea winde brought v néere vnto caſtle gyant tower ſaw v great danger drowning driuen port came downe pallaice ſlewe father except ſelfe ſo brought tower whereas haue béen theſe seauen yeares great diſtreſſe miſerie nowe coozen pray aduenture hath brought hether ſtrang countrey coozen quoth ſéeing knowe aduentures ſhal ſhew troth king charlemaine hath ſent mee meſſuage admirall gaudiſe babilon beare meſſuage mouth letter way lay come tower demaunded paynim within tower anſweared ſayd howe héere ſhould bée great horrible gyant hath done much euill haue paſſed way thought paſſe way fight deſtroy deliuer countrey haue left companie héere valley tarie deare coozen quoth ſhe haue great maruaile would take ſuch folly ye fiue hundred men together well armed yée durſt abide hée armed armour none endure againſt therefore coſin counſell returne backe againe ere doe awake ſhall open wicket ſo ſhall paſſe without danger chap xxxii ¶how damſell coſen huon ſhewed chamber whereas gyant ſlept went waked good armour gyant deliuered huon huon well vnderſtood damſell ſaid coſen know troth ere depart hence ſée man ſhall neuer ſaid reproch court prince feare miſcreant ſhould ſo faint courage durſt abide certainly rather die ſuch fault ſhould come ah coſen quoth ſhée ſée well deſtroyed ſéeing thus ſhall ſhew chamber whereas ſléepeth yée haue ſéene yet yée may returne firſt goe chamber ſée héere wherein yée ſhall find bread wine victual next ſhall find clothes ſilke many rich iewels third quoth huon god ſhall neuer ſaid diſgrace ſhould ſtrike man without knowledge huon departed ladie ſword hand helmet head ſhield necke ſo entred firſt chamber ſecond third wheras ſaw foure god well alſo chamber hanged rich clothes floare couered carpet whē huon well regarded well conſidered gyant xvij foote length body fourniſhed thereafter member fowler hideous creature neuer ſéene great head great eares camelled noſe eye burning like candle ah good lord quoth huon would king charlemaine héere ſée v twoo fight ſure ere departed peace ſhould made lord god humbly require thée ſuccour againſt enemy thy good pleaſure againſt endure huon fiercely aduanced foorth made ſigne croſſe caſting mind might doe thought ſlew ſléeping ſhould great reproch would ſaid ſlaine man dead whereupon ſaid bedſted lay vpon ſaid huon frend ſent thée hether loued thée little doubted huon heard gyant ſpeake french great maruaile ſaid come hether ſee thee may ſo haue done vnaduiſedly gyant ſaid thou ſayeſt troth armed thou art fiue hundred men ſuch thou art could endure yt ſhould die thou ſeeſt naked without ſword weapon yet doubt thée huon thought himſelfe would great ſhame aſſaile man without armour weapon wherefore ſaid goe arme thée incontinent ſhall ſlay thée fréend quoth gyant thou ſayeſt procéedeth good courage courteſie armed tooke hand great fawchin huon withdrawne pallaice abiding gyant tarried long came huon ſaid art thou behould héere ready deſtroy thée without thou make good defence yet deſire thee tell thou art thintent may haue ſlaine thée tell haue ſlaine ſuch one folly came aſſaile myne owne pallaice great pride thée thou wouldeſt ſtrike ere armed whoſoeuer thou art thou ſéemeſt ſonne noble man pray thée ſhew mee whether thou wouldeſt goe mooued thée come hether thintent might know troth thine enterprize haue ſlaine thee may make vaunt men haue ſlaine ſuch man thought ſcorne diſdaine ſtrike ere armed paynim quoth huon thou art great folly thou ſo raſhly reputeſt dead ſeing thou wouldſt know troth poore knight whome king charlemaine hath taken land baniſhed realme fraunce hath ſent doe meſſuage admirall gaudiſe babilon name huon sonne duke seuin bourdeaux haue ſhewed troth mine enterprize pray thée tell thou wert borne engendred thée thintent haue ſlaine thée may make mine auaunt king charles court frends haue ſlaine ſuch maruaylous great gyant thou art ye giant ſaid thou ſlay thou maieſt well make thy vaunt thou haſt ſlaine angolofer gyant hath xvij brother whome yongeſt alſo thou maieſt ſay vnto drie trée red ſea man tributarie haue chaced admirall gaudiſe whome thou ſaieſt thou goeſt haue taken puiſſance diuers city doth yéerely ſeruage tender ring gould buy heade withall alſo tooke oberon fayrie king puiſſant towre enchaunting fayries could reſiſt alſo tooke rich armour thou neuer heardſt ſuch another hath ſuch vertue whoſoeuer put neuer wearie diſcōfited another eſpeciall vertue muſt weare armour muſt without ſpot deadly ſinne alſo mother muſt without carnall copulation man except owne huſband beléeue cannot found man may weare armour alſo ſuch vertue whoſoeuer hath bodye cannot grieued neither fire water mahoūd haue prooued becauſe haue found ſuch courteſie thee thou gaueſt leaue arme giue thee leaue aſſay thou canſt put armour regard know neither thou knight elſe able doe gyant went coffer tooke armour came huon ſaid see heere good armour giue thee leaue aſſay put thy body huon tooke armour went back little put owne armour tooke belonging ye gyant incontinent bodie haſtily put helmet tooke ſhéeld ſword hand deuoutly thanked lord god great grace gyant ſaid mahound little thought thou hadſt ſuch man armour becommeth thee exceeding well nowe haue quit courteſie thou ſhewedſt mee therefore pray thee put armour deliuer againe ſo ſir leaue anſweared huon armour meeter ſuch helhound thou art therefore know troth render againe xiiij beſt city parys friend quoth gyant ſeing thou wilt render againe armour content let thee depart hence without hurt damage alſo giue thée ring gould admirall gaudiſe gaue know well ſtand thee good ſtead thou thinkeſt fourniſh thy meſſuage thou comeſt gate pallaice ſayſt thou art meſſenger ſent frō kyng charles thou ſhalt find foure gate euery gate foure porter ſo firſt gate knowen thou frenchman one thy hand ſhalbe cut ſecond gate thy hand third gate one thy féet fourth foote ſhalt thou bee brought admirall thy head ſtriken therfore eſcape theſe peril furniſh thy meſſuage thintent thou maieſt ſurely retourne giue againe armour ſhall giue ring gold thou ſheweſt thou ſhalt receiued great honor euery gate thou maiſt go retourne ſurelye pallaice thy pleaſure man let thee thou hadſt ſlaine fiue hundred men ſhalbe none ſo hardy touch thée doe thee yll thou haſt ring thée haue nede men mony cannot lacke ſend ring token therfore pray thee let haue againe armour chap xxxiii ¶ huon ſlew rhe great gyant called gerames company ioy made death gyant huon vnderſtoode paynim ſaid ah thou fell falſe deceiuer know troth preacher betwéen eaſt weſt preached whole yeare thou wouldeſt giue thou haſt thy ring therewith would render againe good armour bodie firſt ſlay thée thy ring thou praiſeſt ſo much likewiſe haue whether thou wilt gyant well heard huon ſaw wiſe could get againe armour ſorowfull becauſe ſaw huon reprooued therewith ſo ſore diſpleaſed eye ſéemed like twoo burning candels yet demaunded huon would doe none otherwiſe truly quoth huon though thou great ſtrong haue feare thée ſeing haue good armour therefore name god diuine puiſſance defie thée thée quoth gyant armour thou canſt endure againſt gyant approched huon lift vp fawchin thinking haue ſtriken fayled ſtroke glent fawchin light vpon piller entred twoo foot huon quicke light behoulding maruaylous ſtroke quickly ſtept foorth good ſword hand ſeing gyant fawchin ſticking faſt piller ſtrake gyant ye armes néere hand ſuch wiſe ſtrake hand ſo fawchin fell downe earth gyant felt himſelfe ſo ſore hurt paine therof gaue maruaylous crie ſo horrible though towre fallen earth whereat damſell sibylla chamber ſore abaſhed ſhe went chamber found ſtaffe way ſhe tooke vp hand came pallaice whereas ſhe heard cry met gyant flying away ſaue himſelfe damſell well aduiſed ſhe ſaw fled ſhe caſt ſtaffe betwéene legges ſo thereby fell earth huon came ſword hand haſted gaue gyant many great ſtroke gyant cryed ſo high terrible heare huon lift vp ſword gaue ſuch ſtroake necke head flew earth huon wiped ſword put vp ſheath came head thinking haue taken vp haue ſet height towre head ſo great heauy could remooue tourne bodie ſmiled ſaid ah good lord thanke thée thy grace thou haſt giuen puiſſance ſlay ſuch creature would god body head nowe pallaice parys charlemaine kinge fraunce ſo knewe haue ſlaine huon went window looked ſaw company ſaid hie sir come vp hether ye may doe ſurely pallaice woonne gyant ſlaine gerames garyn heard ioyfull thanked lord god came gate sybilla damſell went ye haue heard huon conquered giant great ioy companie next day huon called together ſaid sir yée knowe well enterprize haue taken doe touching admyrall gaudiſe ▪ therefore conuenient ſhortly doe charlemaine péeres fraunce ſhew hard aduentures haue gone perfourme meſſuage companie vnderſtood would depart ſorowfull ſaide sir yée deſire v tarrie héere xv day know troth wée ſhall tarrie héere whole yéere sir quoth thanke made readie depart armed tooke cuppe horne alſo gyants ring put arme kiſt cooſen others made great lamentation departing went vp pallaice looked windowes huon long might ſée huon went foorth till came ſeaſide farre caſtle little hauen whereas alwaies wont lye ſome manner ſhip veſſell paſſe ouer sea huon came thether though nowe inſtant none finding meanes paſſage ſaid ah good lord ſhall doe finde heere boate veſſell paſſe ala ill houre ſlew charlot wherby thus ſtill danger howbeit mine owne defence great wrong therefore king charles hath done baniſh mine owne countrey theſe like complaint made huon alone began ſore lament ſodainly right hand ſaw great beaſt come ſwimming towards like beare huon beheld made himſelfe ſigne croſſe drew ſwoord defend himſelfe thinking beaſt would haue aſſailed went little huon ſhooke himſelfe ſuch wiſe ſkinne fell faire man well fourmed could ſéene huon great feare maruaile ſaw beaſt become man yet approached neere demaunded whether humane creature el ill ſpirite come thether tempt ſaid right nowe thow didſt ſwimme ſea trauerſed great waues guiſe maruailous beaſt charge thee name god thou hurt ſhew thou art beleeue thou art king oberons company huon quoth diſmay thou know thée right well thou art sonne duke seuin bourdeaux royall king oberon hath ſent thee happened breake commaundment wherfore hath condemned xxx yéeres like beaſt sea frend quoth huon lord fourmed truſt thée till paſt red ſea huon quoth mallaborn know troth ſent hether cauſe beare thee whether thou wilt therefore make thee readie recommend thy ſelfe ſauegard lord ieſus chriſt let alone mallaborn entred againe beaſts ſkinne ſaid huon sir mount vpon backe chap xxxv ¶ huon paſſed sea vpon mallaborn bare babilon huon came firſt gate ſo ſecond huon ſawe beaſte enter againe ſkinne hee taried made ſigne ye croſſe prayed god ſaue conduct ſo leapt vpon beaſt entred ye sea ſwamme faſt though bird ſlowen ſo within ſhort ſpace admirall ſaid sir admirall know troth chriſtened meſſenger ſent noble king charlemaine thée bicauſe prince chriſtian heathē obeyeth cōmaundement except thy ſelfe therefore hee ſendeth thee worde ſince dolorous day battaile ronceuaux whereas loſt twoo nephew rowland oliuer neuer ſince aſſembled ſo much people next ſommer come vpon thée water land without thou wilte beleue lawe ieſus chriſt therefore thou wilt beléeue chriſtened elſe miſchiefe fall vpon thée speake quoth admirall rather hewen ſlaine leaue law beléeue vpon thy god sir admirall quoth huon moreouer king charles commaundeth thée ſend sparhawkes goſhawkes beares wayters chayned together yong varlet faire damſels alſo handfull thy beard foure thy great téeth ha quoth admirall ſée thou art hardy outragious demaund thou haſt ſaid alſo haue great maruaile thy maiſter ſo fooliſh commaund thee ſend beard great téeth time hath ſent xv meſſengers hath demaunded part thou ſpeakeſt xv haue hanged nowe thou art come thy folly make vp xvj reaſon ring thou beareſt dare touch thée pray thée therefore faith law thou art ſhewe mee diuell hath giuen thée ring huon ſore abaſhed durſt make lye feare king oberon ſaid sir doubt thée paynim héere ſpare ſhew thee troth know good ſword haue ſlaine lord angolofer gyant ye admirall heard ſaid lord sir looke villaine eſcape god beléeue ſhall neuer haue ioy heart vntill ſée takē paynim sarazins part aſſayled huon ſaw commended himſelfe lord god thought ſhould neuer ſée faire day ſo ſword hand defended himſelfe nobly ſlaying cutting handes féete sarazins many made braynes flye abroad ye pauement great terrour behould reaſon good armour paynim could damage gaue way durſt approch néere huon full yre fought ſaw one ſide pallaice arch wall ſo euer ſtill fighting drew thether ſet backe arch thintent none ſhould come behind fared like wilde boare wood▪ defended himlelfe ſuch wiſe whome ſoeuer touched full ſtroke néede ſurgeon thus long ſpace huon endured great harme force paynim ſo chap xl ¶ gerames company departed tower damſell came babilon manner gerames vſed know ſome newes huon haue heard heere huon departed tower gyant left gerames company ye damſell coozen taried iij moneths neuer heard thing huon wherof ſorowfull went foorth one morning came seaſide ſée might heare newes lord huon looked vpon sea eſpied ſhippe charged xxx paynim great rich gerames ſaw ſhip coming port wherfore ſaid company sir let v go ſee learne tiding • huon went port time maryners caſt anchor gerames demaunded whence whither would go sir quoth would goe meſque pay angolofer great gyant tribute bound euery yeere pay therefore sir deſire ſhew v might find gerames ſaw land ſhip ſaid ah ye vnhappie paynim ye ſhall neuer depart hence ye demaund dead ye ſhall beare companie▪ gerames ſaide company ſirs let theſe paynim ſlaine incontinent ſet vpon thē ſo paynim ſlaine one eſcaped aliue chriſtian men armed paynim without armour weapon otherwiſe durſt come land feare gyant gerames entred ſhip tooke found bare tower went dinner made great ioy aduenture dinner gerames ſaid sir wee fraunce king charlemaine ſhould demaund v become huon yée know wel none v tel whether aliue dead ſhould ſay dead afterward retourne home ſhould reputed falſe men euer child man may priſoner xiiij xv yeeres yet come home againe laſt ſafe ſound ſirs yee ruled ſhall doe like true men haue port good ſhip well fourniſhed euery thing haue heere gould ſiluer plentie ſhall ſoone vittaile ſhip let v take sea neuer reſt ſayling vntill wee heare ſome newes lord huon doe thus wée doe true men ought doe deſire euery man ſhew aduice herein without taking longer reſpite anſwered one voice readie accompliſh deuiſed tooke gould ſiluer rich bare ſhippe fourniſhed wine biſket ſalt fleſh artillerie ſhippe foure great téeth cut beard tooke therof much pleaſed oberon ſaid thou haſt thy hand admiral téeth beard looke well thou loueſt thy life thou keepe well sir quoth huon require put ſuch place may bee well kept ſo may haue againe time need feele ſelfe heart ſo light either ſhal forget thē elſe loo • e thou ſaieſt quoth oberon thinke thou ſpeakeſt wiſely therefore doe wiſh gerames ſide ſuch manner ſhall doe hurt ſooner ſpoken word god ye power fayrie cloſed gerames ſide ſuch wiſe man could ſée ſaid huon friend muſt goe caſtle momur deſire doe well yée ſhall take eſcleremond daughter admirall charge paine life much yee feare diſpleaſe ye ſo hardy company bodily vntill yée • e married together citie roome thou doeſt contrarie thou ſhalt find ſuch pouertie miſerie though thou hadſt double miſchéefe thou haſt hadde •• nce thou cameſt fraunce yet nothing regard ſhall fall thée hereafter thou breake commaundement sir quoth huon pleaſure lord ieſus chriſt ſhall well beware thing againſt pleaſure oberon apparelled rich ſhippe well garniſhed chamber hanged ſo richly incredible heard ſeene cord gould ſilke ſhould ſhew beautie rich ſhippe would ouer long recite ſhippe fourniſhed vittailes put therein horſes oberon tooke leaue huon kiſſed embraced greatly lamenting huon ſaw wéepe great maruaile ſaid deare sir cauſe doe weepe huon quoth thing mooueth thus bicauſe haue great pitie thée thou kneweſt pouertie miſerie thou ſhalt endure member thou haſt would tremble feare know certen thou haſt ſo much ſuffer humane tongue rehearſe oberon departed without ſpeaking huon ſawe oberon depart right penſiue ſwéetnes youth put ſorow hee made ordinance citie chriſtened faire ladie eſcleremond afterward marrie couſin sibilla admirall countrey newly chriſtened huon gaue thē citie babylon longed thereto made ordayned little ſhip goe owne ſhip thintent ſend land vittailes need ſhould require companie went great ſhip ſo tooke leaue couſin newly married right ſorowfull departing ſet vp ſayles good faire wind ſo ſayled till riuer nyle ſo paſſed damieta came high ſea wind day ſat dinner made good chéere reaſon cup wine pleaſure ah good lord quoth huon greatly bound thanke king oberon haue ſuch cup horne armour whenſoeuer ſhall blowe horne haue men ynough come aide alſo haue admiral • eard great téeth ſpecially faire ladie eſcleremond whome loue ſo perfectly ſo enamoured faire body longer endure dwarffe oberon mocke hath forbidden ſtrictly ſhould touch wiſe well know caſe obey ſhe mine therfore pleaſure gerames heard ſaid ala ſir yée doe yée know well oberon neuer yet made lye alwaies ye haue found true hee ſo wée béene loſt time againe would breake commaundement yee touch ladie ere time come hath ſet great miſfortune ſhall f • thereby gerames quoth huon forbeare ere depart haue pleaſure affraid content ſhall depart little ſhip goe liſt take vittaile prouiſion sir quoth gerames ſéeing yée doe none otherwiſe right ſorowfull depart ſo companie gerames departed great ſhippe entred little ſhippe xiij companie huon tarried ſtill ladie ſaw company departed went made readie bed ſaid ladie madame ſurely muſt haue pleaſure ſhee heard huon ſhée fell downe ſore weeping humbly deſired huon would forbeare companie vntill • time ſhould married together according promiſe made king oberon faire ladie quoth huon ▪ excuſes auaile muſt thus tooke ladie made goe bed tooke together pleaſures ſooner accompliſhed aroſe ſuch maruailous tempeſt waues ſea ſéemed ſo great high mountaines therewith blew thundred lightned fearefull behould ſea ſhippe ſo ſore tormented burſt péeces ſo remained one péece timber whereuppon huon ladie happened ſo well néere iſle thither winde draue ſaw arriued land kneeled downe thanked lord ieſus chriſt ſo well eſcaped perill drowning pitiouſly weeping entred • iſle wheras dwelt neither man woman earth ſo faire gréen great ioy ſée likewiſe ſo faire hot hid ſelues greene graſſe thintent ſhould perceaued ſtill lady wept pitiouſly huon ſaid vnto lady bée abaſhed dye loue wée ſhall firſt triſtram died loue faire iſoluda ſhée ſo wéeping clipped kiſſed eche lay wrapped gréene graſſe ariued tenne sarazins litle veſſell entred iſle take freſh water thing needed ſaid eche let v goe foorth iſle ſee wée find aduenture theſe men pyrates ſea ſerued admirall gaudiſe father eſcleremond huon louer gréen graſſe heard neere people comming hée thought go ſée might get meate deere louer quoth huon pray goe hence till returne sir quoth ſhée god guide requyre returne againe ſhortely hee departed naked borne ſo came thē dyned ſaluted deſired humbly loue god gyue hym ſome bread one aunſwered ſaide fréend thou ſhalt haue ynough pray thee ſhew v aduenture hath brought thee hether sir quoth huon tempeſt ſea hath brought hether ſhippe periſhed companye heard great pity gaue two loaues bread huon tooke departed thanking went backe loue gaue parte bread whereof ſhée little glad pyrates giuen huon bread ſaid one another man thus gone v ſurely yt hath ſome company therfore let v goe preſently peraduenture wée ſhall finde company mee thinkes alone hée would ſo haue come v let v go ſée quoth returne till know troth went together followed huon priuilie could came néere whereas hée ſaw ladie hard eating bread giuen ſtood ſtill aduiſed ſée could haue knowledge lady among one ſaid sir neuer beleue mée ladie faire eſcleremond daughter admirall gaudiſe hée ſame frenchmā fought agrapart ſlew alſo admirall happy haue found ſpecially naked without armour armed lyues ſhort knew certainely eſcleremond daughter admirall gaudiſe ye ſhalbe example leachour ſhalbe ſlayne face lady ſaw theſe paynim ſhe • right ſorowfull ſore diſcomforted ſhe kneled held vp hir handes prayed humbly would haue pitie frenchman owne life ſhée put owne pleaſures either ſlay hir drowne elſe bring vncle ſirs quoth ſhee ſweare mahound ye grant requeſt agreed mine vncle iuorin ſhall doe ſuch pleaſures ye ſhall rich euer little ſhall yee winne death one poore man ladie quoth well content leaue héere wée ſhall doe ſhame rebuke hee may remember euer tooke huon laide grene graſſe blind eies binde hand féet ſo blood burſt nayles wherby hée ſuch ſea admirall galaffer anfalerne deliuered hand ſheweth hiſtorie theſe théeues takē bound huons hand féet eyen left alone iſle tooke faire eſcleremond brought hir ſhippe gaue hir gowne mantell furred ermyns robber ſea much good ſhippe ſayled foorth night day laſt wind tooke whether would arriued port anfalerne ſame time admirall newly riſen dinner ſtood leaning window pallaice hée perceiued ſhippe ſirs pray tell mee damſell ſée ſhippe ſore wéeping sir quoth ſlaue chriſtian woman whome bought damieta ladie heard well admirall demaunded likewiſe anſwere mariner made ſhee cried aloud ſaid ala sir admirall loue honour mahound pray haue pitie ſlaue daughter admirall gaudiſe babylon dead ſlaine frenchman mariner heere haue taken would carrie mine vncle king iuoryn mombrance know ſurely would burne faire lady quoth admirall diſmay yee ſhall abide mee whether commaunded mariner bring ladie anſwered would ſo doe admirall commaunded take perforce ſhippe began make defence anon ſlaine lady galaffer whome ſaluted name mahound hee declared meſſuage length aſſoone galaffer heard meſſuage ſaid friend goe ſay king iuoryn deliuerance néece doe men ſlaine owne folly touching ſhould come come long ſpace hée ſomewhat aſſwaged yre hée ſware god mahound hée ſhould neuer haue ioy mirth heart till hee deſtroyed towne anfalerne ſlaine admirall galaffer haſt hée ſent lord concluded ſend men warre gloriant mallaborn monſter sea went ſuccoured huon carried iſle noyſant hiſtorie ſheweth king oberon ſame time huon iſle noyſant wood moſt part hee accuſtomed conuerſant bicauſe ye place much delectable farre people hee ſat downe vnder faire oake hee began weepe complaine gloriant knight fairie ſaw great maruaile demaunded lamented ſo much gloriant quoth king oberon periured huon bourdeaux cauſeth mee thus doe whome haue alwayes perfectly loued yet ſtill treſpaſſeth commandements departed cauſed haue admirall gaudiſe pleaſure alſo made haue faire eſcleremond admiral daughter alſo haue giuen rich horne iuorie good cup hath loſt pride folly therefore hath puniſhed hee lyeth naked bound handes féete eye blindfolded iſle place ſuffer die moſt miſerably ſo sir quoth gloriant honour lord ieſus chriſt call remembrance howe god owne mouth adam eue forbidden eating fruit paradiſe yet fragilitie brake god commaundement howbeit lord god great pitie therefore sir pray haue pitie huon mallaborn ſtept foorth ſayd ala sir honour reuerence lord god deſire graunt one time may goe ayd oberon ſawe ſo earneſtly deſired glorian • mallaborn ſore diſpleaſed anſwearing ſayd mallaborn pleaſeth ſo well caytiffe huon endureth ſo much paine viſited thée therefore condemne thée bee xxviij yeares monſter sea beſide xxx yeares thou art enioyned alreadie thou giueſt none counſaile aid alonely beare iſle ſet maine land let goe whether hée deſire neuer ſee alſo thou bringeſt againe vnto rich horne iuorie rich cup armour fetch hee hath loſt ala sir quoth mallaborn great paine put vnto ſo ſmal offence ſo ſore diſpleaſed huon ye armour would haue againe know well huon bourdeaux conquer hée loſt béene great ill ſhall doe cauſe haue againe sir ſince haue licence bring iſle pray ſhewe mée place iſle whereas gloriant ſayd brother mallaborn iſle néere vnto hell called iſle noyſant well quoth mallaborn commend lord ieſus chriſt ſo departed came ſeaſide came leapt sea began ſwim faſt bird flyeth ayre ſo arriued iſle noyſaunt ſo came vnto huon whome hée found ſore wéeping ſayd sir huon pray lord ieſus chriſt ſuccour aide thée ah deare god quoth huon ſpeaketh vnto huon quoth hée man loueth thée called mallaborn beaſt sea hath time borne thée ouer ſalt water babilon ah mallaborn déere brother quoth huon require thée vnbind mée bring dolorous paine right good quoth mallaborn vnbind opened eye huon ſawe hée right ioyfull demanded ſent thether huon quoth knowe troth king oberon whereas condemned beaſt sea thirtie yeares thy ſake muſt endure ſo eight twentie yeares yet care paine loue beare vnto thée paine impoſſible vnto mée beare muſt carie againe vnto oberon rich horne cup armour ſo haue promiſed king oberon doe ah quoth huon pray lord ieſus chriſt confound dwarfe hath cauſed endure theſe paine ſo ſmall occaſion huon quoth mallaborn doe ill ſay ſo haue ſooner ſpoken king oberon doth know certainly quoth huon care doe hath done ſo much ill neuer loue sir pray thée tell thou wilt beare hence elſe whether muſt abide héere euer fréend quoth mallaborn beare thée iſle ſet thée maine lande ayd may doe thée mallaborn tooke vppon againe beaſts ſkin ſayd sir leape vppon mée huon leapt vppon backe naked euer borne mallaborn leapt sea began ſwim came mayne land ſayd fréend huon ſeruice doe vnto thée time recommend thée kéeping lord god ſend thee comfort muſt goe ſéeke horne cup armor thou wert woont haue enioy beare vnto king oberon thus haue promiſed doe huon alone naked pitiouſly complayning ſayde ah good lord require thée ayde mée know whether may goe yet cloathes couer naked ſkinne ſhould haue ſome comfort might goe ſéeke ſome aduenture greatly ought hate crooked dwarfe oberon hath brought paine faith yt owe vnto god ſéeing hath left thus hencefoorth doe ſpite ſhall make kéepe companie ſhall find ſorowfull man faith quoth huon companion owne ſort haue found neuer man ſuffered ſo much pouertie haue praiſe vnto fourmed ſéeing haue found meat eat bleſſed houre haue found left caſe ſhewe troth life man dead ſhall neuer truſt thée put truſt god loue haue loue thou haſt mee hate ſéeing ſo often haue néede ſhall ly ſhall leaue feare thée rather deſpite thée huon ſaide minſtrell sir haue demanded mine eſtate yet haue made none anſweare troth find ſelfe ſo well mine eaſe forgat anſweare ſhall nowe ſhewe ſéeing would know sir certaine borne countrey affricke fell company diuers marchants sea shippe thinking haue ſayled damieta great miſfortune fell vppon v aroſe ſuch horrible tempeſt shippe periſhed within none eſcaped thanke mahound eſcaped aliue therefore deſire ſhew mée aduenture haue ſhewed mine fréend quoth minſtrell ſéeing knowe knowe troth named mouflet minſtrell thou ſéeſt héere mine inſtruments ſay vnto thée hence red sea none ſo cunning inſtruments doe many thing dolour thou ſéeſt mee make bycauſe late haue loſte good lorde maiſter admirall gaudiſe ſlayne miſerably vacabond fraunce called huon mahound ſhame bring ill death fallen pouerty miſerie pray thée tell thy name sir quoth huon name solater well quoth minſtrell solater diſmay thée great pouerties thou haſt ſuffered thou ſéeſt aduenture mahound hath ſent thée thou art nowe better arayed thou wert thou wilt follow counſel thou ſhalt haue néed thou art faire young thou oughteſt diſmayed old ancient haue cauſe diſcomforted ſéeing mine olde dayes haue loſt lord maiſter admirall gaudiſe ſo much good profit would pleaſed mahound ſlewe power huon heard ſpake word caſt head solater quoth minſtrell ſéeing lord dead goe mombrance king iuoryn ſhew death brother admirall gaudiſe thou wilt abide ſo thou wilt beare fardell harpe foote ere halfe yéere paſt warrant thée thou ſhalt haue horſe whenſoſeuer thou ſhalt heare play vpon inſtruments hearer ſhall take therein ſuch pleaſure ſhall giue mee gownes mantle ſo thou ſhalt haue much adoe truſſe male well sir quoth huon content ſerue doe commaundements huon tooke male necke harpe hand mouflet maiſter bare vyoll thus good armour horne cup would reckon al ſorrow haue endured nothing xiij knight ſerue chaunce turned ſelfe muſt ſerue poore minſtrell mouflet heard huon make ſuch ſorow within ſelfe hée ſaid déere brother solater take good comfort morow night thou ſhalt ſee good cheere ſhall bee made mée wherof thou ſhalt haue part goodes get maiſter quoth huon mahound reward goodnes ye haue ſhewed mée ſhall thus maiſter ſeruant went foorth together deuiſing laſt huon eſpied behind coming certē men armes houlding waye mombrance maiſter quoth huon héere behind v coming men armour know whether doe v hurt solater quoth mouflet bee abaſhed wee abide héere know whether goe within man war came number fiue c perſons minſtrell ſaluted ſaid sir pray ſhewe mee whether ye goe frend quoth one bicauſe ſée ye gentle minſtrell ſhall ſhew going king iuoryn mombrance néeds goe make warre vppon admirall galaffer bicauſe late damſell eſcleremond daughter admirall gaudiſe paſſed anfalerne ſhould haue béen admirall galaffer haue ſhewed cauſe going citie mombrance chap lii ¶ huon maiſter mouflet arriued mombrance huon ſpake king iuoryn huon bourdeaux vnderſtood paynim going ladie eſcleremond ſurprized ioy ſaid maiſter sir require lette v goe warres solater quoth mouflet beware thou ſayeſt warre would come thing thus went foorth vntill came mombrance went ſtraight pallaice whereas found king iuoryn baron minſtrell ſaw hee ſaluted name mahound ſayde sir right dolorous newes bring sir brother lord maiſter admirall gaudiſe pitiouſly ſlayn mouflet quoth iuoryn theſe newes hath béen brought vnto mée time whereof much agréeued alſo ſorrie néece faire eſcleremond kept mée admirall galaffer meſſuage ſend ſend backe mée ye faith owe god mahound ſhall make ſuch warre memorie thereof ſhall bee hundred yeares héereafter ſhall leaue neuer foote land ſhall bring fire flame cleane deſtroy deſpite téeth ſée neece eſcleremond may get ſhall cauſe ſtriken al péeces burne aſhes brother dead villaine fraunce vppon whome ſhée amourous huon heard ſpeake lady heart roſe made promiſe himſelfe ere moneth paſt would goe ſée find meanes ſpeake king iuoryn called mouflet minſtrell ſayd fréend pray thée doe ſome thinge make mée merrie reaſon diſpleaſure haue ioy loſt therefore better take ſome mirth bee long ſorrow sir quoth mouflet readie doe pleaſure hée tooke vyoll playd thereof ſuch wiſe great melodie heare al paynim great ioy mirth made great feaſting huon heard ſaid good lord require thée great ioy may turne mée heare ſome good newes deſire ſo ſore ſée minſtrell finiſhed ſong paynim cloathes ſome gaue gownes ſome mantle hee thought himſelfe right well happie could giue minſtrell thing huon ynough doo gather together cloathes giuen hée put male whereof huon ioyfull bicauſe ſhould haue one halfe king iuoryn beheld huon ſayd vnto great dammage ſo faire younge man ſhould ſerue minſtrell sir quoth mouflet abaſhed though young man doe ſerue hee hath cauſe ſo doe brother dead departed thence come hether way found great dake vnder ſat downe reſt great fountaine faire cleare ſpread abroad towell graſſe ſet thereon bread ſuch meate drinke ſame time young man arriued came vnto mee naked prayed loue mahound giue ſome bread ſo cloathed ſée ſo much promiſed ſerue mée beare fardell harpe moreouer came paſſage water hee would caſt necke light though béen nothing ſo ſtrong beare ouer ah poore catiffe quoth king iuoryn haſt thou liued ſo longe cannot perceiue doth abideth vntill thou haſt gotten ſome rich cut thy threat caſt thée riuer goe away thy rich cauſe come ſpeake mée sir quoth mouflet hée ſhall come ſo called huon brought king iuoryn fréend quoth king pray thée ſhewe thou wert borne haue pitie thée ſée thée ſo low eſtate bee varlet minſtrell better thée ſerue ſome prince helpe kéepe towne caſtle rather thus looſe thy time wote ſhould thinke therein ſéemeth mee thou art faint courage hath mooued thée thus doe thou ſéeeſt thy maiſter hath nothing hee getteth vyoll canſt thou find none meanes liue honeſtly sir quoth huon craft ynow ſhall name vnto heare say quoth iuoryn haue great deſire know thou canſt one thing aduiſe thée make vaunt thing without thou canſt doe indéede euerie thinge prooue thée sir quoth huon mew sparrowhauke chaſe hart wilde boare blow prize ſerue hound right ſerue table great prince play cheſſe table aſwell doe neuer found man could winne liſt chap liii ¶ king iuoryn cauſed daughter play cheſſe huon vpon condition mated ſhould looſe head ſhee mated huon ſhould haue loue huon wonne game king ivorin heard huon ſaid hould thée ſhall prooue whether true thou ſaieſt yet sir quoth huon pray let mee ſhew farther doe aſſay mee pleaſure mahound quoth king content thou ſhalt ſhew thou canſt doe sir quoth huon right well arme ſet helmet head beare ſhield ſpeare runne gallop horſe commeth point ſtrokes ſhould giuen yée may well ſend foorth worſe alſo sir right well enter lady chamber embrace kiſſe doe ſeruice friend quoth iuoryn heare thée thou canſt doe thing ſhould turne good prooue thée ſhall cauſe thee aſſayed play cheſſe haue faire daughter whome thou ſhalt play vpon condition ſhe winne thou ſhalt looſe thy head thou canſt mate promiſe thée thou ſhalt haue thy wife repoſe thy pleaſure c markes money therewith sir quoth huon pleaſure▪ would glad forbeare enterpriſe mahound quoth king ſhalbe none otherwiſe come thereof meane ſeaſon bargaine making paynim went lady chamber ſhewed king father young man made promiſe ſhould play cheſſe vpon condition loſt game hee ſhould looſe head chaunced win haue wedded wife c markes money madame quoth aſſure ſhall play againſt faireſt man euer ſaw pitie ſhould varlet minſtrell mahound quoth ladie hould father foole thinketh ſhould ſuffer man die winning game cheſſe iuoryn ſent daughter twoo king brought ye king father iuoryn ſaid daughter thou muſt play cheſſe young varlet thou ſeeſt héere ſo thou winne ſhall looſe head winne hee ſhall thy huſband doe thee pleaſure father quoth ladie ſéeing pleaſure reaſon doe whether ſhee beheld huon whome ſhee ſaw right faire ſaid ſelfe mahound great beautie ſee young man would game end ſo wedded wife ladie come place made redie ſhee huon ſat downe king iuoryn baron ſat downe ſée play huon ſaid king sir require none doe ſpeake game neither one partie friend quoth king haue doubt thereof ſuretie king cauſed proclaymed thorow pallaice none ſhould ſo hardie ſpeake one word vpon paine death cheſſe made readie huon ſaide ladie game yée play friend quoth ſhe game accuſtomed mated corner began ſtudie firſt draught paynim beheld huon cared ſtudied game begun ſo huon loſt moſt parte pawnes wherewith changed colour bluſhed redde roſe damſell perceiued ſaid friend whereon doe yée thinke yee almoſt mated anon father ſtrike head madame quoth yet game done great ſhame ſhall father haue yée ſhall lye night mine armes ſeruant poore minſtrell baron heard huon ſay ſo began laugh ladie ſo ſurpriſed loue huon regard great beautie ſhe ſaw ſhe forgat play thinke whereby ſhe loſt game whereof huon right ioyfull called king ſaid sir may yée ſée play would ſtudie little could mate daughter whereas liſt king ſaw ſaid daughter ariſe curſed houre begate thee great diſhonour haſt thou done heretofore haſt mated ſo many great men ſee heere face minſtrels varlet hath mated thée sir quoth huon trouble ſelfe cauſe wager ſhould winne therby content releaſe quite let daughter goe chamber ſport damſels pleaſure ſhall goe ſerue maiſter minſtrell friend quoth king thou wilt ſhew courteſie ſhall giue thée hundred markes money sir quoth huon content pleaſure ladie went way ſorowfull ſaid ſelfe ah falſe ſainted heart mahound confound thee knowen thou wouldeſt thus haue refuſed companie would haue mated thée thou hadſt loſt thy head thus matter paſſed till next day king iuorin made proclamation citie euerie man ſhould armed mounted horſes minde ſet forward towards enemy euerie man armed mounted horſes many helmet glittered againſt ſunne many trompets drum began ſound ſuch brute made within citie maruaile heare chap liiii ¶ huon armed mounted poore horſe went armie anfalerne huon ſaw wherwith arme heart mourned right ſore gladly hee woulde haue gone foorth might haue horſe haue ridden wherefore hee came king iuoryn ſaid sir require let mee haue horſe armour may goe battaile ſhall yee ſée aid friend quoth iuoryn content ye goe king commaunded one chamberlaines deliuer horſe armour chamberlaine ſaid sir beware yee doe oftentimes ſuch flying vagabounds light courage haue horſe armour may aſſoone goe enemy part kéepe neuer truſt ſome counterfeit varlet king heard ſay ſo ſaide may well bee yet let haue good armour helmet ſhéeld let horſe ſmall valew intent ſhall goe farre though would ſame time paynim heard king grant huon ſhould haue armour went houſe tooke coffer old ruſty ſword brought huon ſaid frend ſée wéell yée haue ſword aid ſelfe withall therefore giue ſword haue long kept coffer paynim giue huon mockery thought ſword ſmall value huon tooke ſword drew ſheath ſaw letter written thereon french ſaying ſword forged galams dayes forged thrée ſwords ſame ſword one three ſecond called durandell third courtayn huon read letter right ioyfull ſaid paynim friend good ſwoord yee haue geuen mee thanke promis may liue long ſhall reward double valew therof huon ſword brought vnto good armour helmet ſhéeld ſpeare ruſty head huon cared little reaſon great deſire hee come ye place whereas hee might ſhew ſtrength vertue thē brought leane horſe pilled long necke great head huon ſaw horſe tooke brydle leapt vpon without foote ſtirrop ſight paynim preſent ſome ſaid well done giue horſe could ſerue aid time need huon mounted leane féeble horſe hée ſorowfull well hee perceaued mocked ſaid ſoftly ſelfe ah yee falſe paynim may lyue yeere ſhall quitte mockes huon rode foorth others hee could doe ſpurres horſe would goe ſoft pace wherat diuers paynim mocked thus king iuoryn departed mombrance great armie tarried field men aſſembled together hee departed tooke way anfalerne diſtant foure league came ran citie draue away beaſtes béeues mutton ſent mombrance admirall galaffer ſaw king iuoryn citie driuen away pray aboute towne ſo ſorowfull hee neere hand wit hée ſaw faire eſcleremond ſaid madame great loue haue ſet day derely bought occaſion ſée country deſtroyed men ſlayne handes vntill haue pleaſure sir quoth ſhée may mee ſhall pleaſe twoo yeares bee paſt accompliſhing vow madame quoth galaffer render vncle iuoryn ſhall haue neuer foot land firſt ſhall cleane diſtroyed chap lv ¶ huon fought sorbryn ſlew wanne good horſe blanchardyn whereon mounted wan battaile brought great tryumph mombrance sorbryn nephew admiral galaffer heard vncle make ſuch ſorow hée ſaid faire vncle diſmayed though iuoryn hath taken ſlaine ſome men driuen away beaſtes eche one lyue ſhall render againe foure ſhall tell goe arme iſſue ſhew iuoryn hee ſet one twoo hardieſt men hoaſt fight ſo ouercome render faire néece eſcleremond pleaſure diſcomfite men let depart ſo damage hath done warre hee render againe double thereof better warre ſhould end two men rather ſo much people ſhould deſtroyed faire nephew quoth galaffer neuer heard better word well content ye haue thus sorbryn went armed ſelfe goodly knight ye paynim land péere none approched neere valiantnes hée armed blanchardyn good horſe brought goodnes horſe excéeded beautie none like white ſnowe freſhnes apparell ſo riche goodly cannot make due mention thereof man could eſtéeme valew rich brydle ſaddle harneſſe sorbryn leapt vppon horſe without ſtirroppe tooke great ſpeare ſo rode cittie hée ſaw king iuoryn farre hée cryed aloud ſaid ah thou iuoryn mombrance admirall galaffer hath ſent mee thée willeth thou doe arme one thy valianteſt men thy court let come againſt hee vanquiſh hee ſhall deliuer thée thy néece eſcleremond ouercome thy man thou retourne thy citie ſuffer thy neece remaine ſtill alſo thou reſtore damage thou haſt done warre iuoryn heard paynim looked ſée men would take enterpriſe fight sorbryn paynim durſt ſpeake one word feared sorbryn fiercenes ſaid amonge themſelues whoſoeuer fight againſt like miſerably finiſh dayes ſame time iuorin ſpake sorbrin huon among paynim heard sorbryn ſaid alſo ſaw yt man durſt goe againſt sorbryn well hée might got himſelfe preſſe vpon leane horſe ſtrake ſpurres hée could doe horſe would neither trot gallop go ſtill pace old minſtrell beheld huon varlet made readie fight againſt paynim ſaw ſo ill horſed cryed hye ſayd sir king iuoryn ſhalbe vnto great diſhonour ſuch horſe nothing woorth haue deliuered vnto varlet gooth ſake fight sorbryn whome none men dare fight great ſinne hath better horſe huon ſayd vnto sorbryn sarazin pray thée ſpeake fréend quoth sorbryn wilt thou mée paynim quoth huon require thée prooue thy vertue againſt mée quoth sorbryn tell mée art thou paynim sarazin fréend quoth huon neither paynim sarazin chriſtened beléeuing ye law ieſus chriſt though thou ſéeſt mée poorely apparelled deſpiſe come noble extraction wherefore require thée thy lawe thou beléeueſt let mée goe without battaile fréend quoth sorbryn requeſt thou doeſt great folly thou deſireſt thy death haue pitie thée therefore councell thée returne backe paynim quoth huon rather dy returne ere haue iuſted thée went take courſe euer huon could doe horſe would aduance foorth whereof huon ſore diſpleaſed ſayd ah verie god man deſire thée giue mée grace may winne horſe paynim doth ryde vppon huon ſaw horſe would neither go forward backwarde hée ſet shéeld againſt enemie sorbryn came running like tempeſt speare ſtrooke huons shéeld ſuch ſtroake buckle thing elſe coulde reſiſt ſtroake sheeld peirced throughout good armour ſaued huon hurt hée remooued ſtroake béen ſtrong wall whereof iuoryn great maruaile ſaid one another neuer ſéene ſo great ſtroake goodlyer receit thereof without falling earth euerie man praiſed greatly huon held himſelfe ſo firmly mahound quoth iuoryn man fierce great hardyneſſe woulde hée mounted vpon horſe huon receiued great ſtroake great yre caſt downe speare tooke sword handes gaue therewith paynim great ſtroake paſſed hye vppon healme ſtroake ſo puiſſant neither healme coiffe ſtéele could reſiſt ſtroake head clouen ſhoulders ſo hee fell downe dead féeld huon quicke light tooke yt good horſe blanchardine reyne alighted horſe without féet ſtirrop leapt vppon paynim horſe left owne féeld hée ſaw himſelfe blanchardine ſmoat ſpurres prooue horſe felt ſpurres hée began leape gambould gallop béen thunder paynim maruell fallen earth ſo whē well prooued turned thought hee would giue value realme hee came vnto king iuoryn twentie gan ••• ulds mahound quoth iuoryn varlet ſéemeth rather sonne king prince varlet minſtrell came vnto huon embraced made great reſpecte paynim within anfalerne admirall galaffer yſſued citie galaffer ſaw nephew ſlain road thrée time made pitious complaint ſaid ah right deare nephewe may well complaine reaſon youth ſée thus pitiouſly ſlaine certainly liue long death ſhall dearely bought ſo cauſed dead bodie carried citie great lamentation hee men entred battaile great ſlaughter made part among huon maruailes ſlew beat downe tare helmet ſtrake braines pummell sword hée ſlew beat downe came within ſtroake proweſſe ſuch paynim durſt abide companie sir wee ariued good port▪ city dwelleth paynim king beléeueth god fierce paynim cannot found frō hence red sea called admirall galaffer without god haue pitie v cannot ſée like die cannot returne backe ſame time admirall galaffer riſen dinner looked windowe behelde ſeaſide perceiued little shippe gerames companie ſaw went downe ſome men deſiring knewe arriued approached shippe ſaid sir men thus arriued port sir quoth gerames wée frenchman pilgrimes going offer holy sepulchre fortune sea hath brought v hether therefore sir tribute ought pay readie pleaſure sir quoth admirall haue doubt mine ſhall haue diſpleaſure yée abide well arriued sir quoth gerames would might pleaſe ſhewe v cauſe quoth admirall ſhall ſhewe true héere néere mée dwelleth kinge iuoryn mombrance maketh vppon mée great warre hée ſlayeth men deſtroyeth countrey whereof haue great ſorrow heart sir quoth gerames quarrell iuſt rightfull ſhall readie aid truely sir without quarrell good wee abide sir quoth admirall ſhall ſhew troth ſo vppon day ſtood window looked downe ye ſeaſide arriued port ſaw shippe comming tooke anker nowe ship damſell ten marriners thought haue ledde vnto kinge iuoryn mombrance cannot tell taken ſhée daughter admirall gaudiſe mahound take ſoule knewe certaine king iuoryn might haue damſell hee would haue burnt becauſe hath béen ſhewed ſhe cauſe death father admirall gaudiſe brother king iuoryn ſo hée vncle damſell aduertiſed ten marriners would haue deliuered hand vncle iuoryn tooke ſlew becauſe would deliuer entreatie thus haue wedded damſell iuoryn heard made mée war héere citie puiſſance hath ſlayne men led away beaſts prouiſion hath burnt deſtroyed countrey euerie day commeth ouerrunnes country hath young man know countrey hee laſt day hée ſlewe nephewe mine whome right dearely loued called sorbryn hée sonne siſter whome haue ſuch ſorrowe heart cannot appeaſed hath led away horſe called blanchardyn beſt horſe ten realmes like world wherefore deſire may deſerue ſeruice abide mée doe ſo much might haue ſaide younge man taken priſoner horſe againe reſtored doe ſhall ſo reward ſhall alwaies rich thoſe companie sir quoth gerames hée come hether ſhewe mée ſhall doe beſt bring horſe alſo vnto freend quoth admirall ſhew courteſie ſhall abandon realme bee pleaſure commaundement theſe word old gerames yſſued ship companie entred citie anfalerne admirall galaffer came pallaice gerames ſayd sir companie require ſhewe v damſell whoſe ſake maintaine war fréend quoth admirall young man would ſhew vnto ſee well bee olde ancient wherefore young ladie ſet thinge admirall tooke gerames hand led chamber whereas eſcleremond aſſoone ladie ſaw gerames ſhe knew wherewith ſhe began chang colour fell ſwound chamber making great outcrie admirall galaffer ſaw right ſorrowfull ſaid faire ladie doe make ſorrow troubled ſight olde man haue brought hether nay ſurely sir quoth ſhée paine hath taken mée right ſide whereby haue often time great annoyance sir pleaſure would gladly ſpeak french knight cuſtomably know many thing peraduēture may ſhew ſuch thing ſhalbe health frenchman right diſcréet giuing good counſell madame quoth admirall pleaſeth well ſpeake ſecretly ladie called gerames ſaid fréend pray thee giue ſome good counſaile may eaſed paine endure madame quoth gerames honour admirall héere preſent ſhall ayd ſuch wiſe ſhalbe eaſed paine endure gerames ſubtill well perceiued mind ladie approached néere vnto ſat downe together couch gerames quoth ladie pray aduenture hath brought hether madame quoth wee bee come hether reaſon tempeſt sea ladie quoth pray become huon faith quoth ſhe beléeue hee dead departed v ſuch maruelous tempeſt roſe sea shippe periſhed ſhip drowned broken ſmall peeces except huon ſaued v table wood wherevpon arriued iſle neere v wée land came vnto v ten marriners tooke thence •• huon blindfold hand féet faſt bound ſo power reléeue himſelfe thoſe ten marriners brought hether admirall galaffer hath ſlayn al therefore thinke ſurely huon dead ieſus haue mercie vppon thus héere admirall hath aſſured wed mée yet neuer medled bodily haue made beléeue made vowe mahound twoo yeares come man ſhould haue vſe body loue huon whome cannot forget admirall hath beleeued long liue ſhall neuer forget huon ſhall alwayes ready die payn kéepe bodily company man liuing ah sir gerames might doe ſo much might eſcape hence ſhould great courteſie might eſcape hence come chriſtian realme would yéeld ſelfe ſome abbie nunnes entent reaſidue life might pray soule louer huon madam quoth gerames diſmayed eſcape hence whatſoeuer come thereof ſhall carie admirall came vnto ſayd fréend hold ouerlong talking damſell come away haue taried long ynough gerames departed eſcleremond ſtrayning hand admirall galaffer tooke together laſte knewe entred anfalerne ſhut admirall without ſheweth hiſtorie twoo dayes king iuoryn made courſe anfalerne huon came vnto iuoryn ſayd sir cauſe men armed let v goe viſite admirall galaffer man warre ought neuer lye ſtill vntill hath brought enemie vtter ruine ſéemeth ſetteth little kéepeth ſtill neece againſt hée subiect one holdeth land freend quoth iuoryn ſay truely ſhall doe counſaile made cryed citie euerie man ſhould make readie go king anfalerne huon deſirous haue battaile armed tooke blanchardyn good horſe mounted without ſtirrop tooke great speare hand good ſharpe head ſame time huon pallaice king iuorins daughter leaning window chamber accompanied diuers lady damſels ſhee beheld huon ſhée ſaid mahound goodly ſight behould yonder young man ſitting horſe blanchardyn well becommeth armour goodlier man cannot found hardie laſt day ſlew sorbryn valianteſt knight pagany alſo wanne good horſe yet diſpleaſed whē played cheſſe ſo hardy embrace kiſſe would haue loued ſuch wiſe required loue would haue refuſed though father ſworne contrarie hundred time thus lady damſels deuiſed together huon ſet little thereby thus king iuoryn men iſſued citie mombrance came field roade foorth toward anfalerne laſt came gate citie ordered battaile array huon great deſire attaine renowne came gate ſpeare hand cried alowd walles ſaid galaffer lord goe ſhew come iuſt gerames friend ſhal ſhew héere hath done al ill ſhall ſée yée kéepe promiſe sir quoth gerames take care faith owe god ſhall render horſe man doe pleaſure gerames yſſued armed well horſed tooke good ſpeare hand hee goodly knight age puiſſant bodie time greatly redoubted horſe hee ſtretched himſelfe ſaddle ſuch wiſe ſtirrops ſtretched long handfull greatly prayſed paynim ſaw admirall galaffer commaunded euery man armed himſelfe armed richly gate opened gerames firſt iſſued company without citie ſtrake horſe ſpurres ſo great ſpace companie ſpeare hand ſhield necke white beard hanging downe breſt vnder helmet nowe huon part ſaw gerames comming hee ſpurred blanchardyn came againſt gerames ſo met together without word ſpeaking ſtrake ſhéeldes ſo broken armour ſo good tooke hurt ſpeares brake handes ſhiuers flew vp ayre ſtroakes ſo rude knight horſes fell earth aroſe againe gaue great ſtroakes gerames expert déedes armes tooke ſword hand gaue huon ſuch ſtroake helmet perforce faine ſet one knées earth ſtroake ſo heauy béen grace god béene ſlaine huon ſo aſtoniſhed ſtroake much adoo recouer ſaid ah good lord ſuccour graunt die maye ſée faire eſcleremond theſe word ſpake openly thought gerames vnderſtood little thought béen gerames yt fought thē came gerames ſword hand haue béen reuenged neuer receiued ſuch ſtroake gerames giuen gerames vnderſtood huon word knew therwith caſt downe ſword earth ſuch ſorow could ſpeake word huon ſaw maruayled greatly caſt ſword earth huon would touch ſaid paynim thy mind doe wilt thou haue peace elſe fight ah ſir quoth gerames come foorth ſtrike head well haue deſerued ſéeing haue ſtricken ſo rudely knew whereof ſory huon heard ſpeake anon knew well gerames wherof great ioy heart finding paynim regarded hadde great maruaile thing twoo champion ment thought sir quoth gerames behooueth v ſhortly determine buſineſſe ſée part paynim aſſemble together behould v ſhall ſhew beſt v twoo doe leape vpon horſe ſhall leape mine ſhall take lead perforce priſoner citie anfalerne ſhall yée ſée loue eſcleremond haue great ioy comming ſhée tell newes friend quoth huon ſhall doe yee deuiſe leapt horſes gerames came huon laid hand though tooke priſoner ſo led toward citie anfalerne companie followed king iuoryn ſawe gerames led away huon priſoner began crie ſaid forth yée sarazins ſuffer yong man led away priſoner ye citie anfalerne ſhall neuer haue ioy heart ye ſuffer thus ledde away sarazins daſhed preaſſe haue reſcued huon part admirall galaffer came met gerames huon gerames ſaid sir goe fight enemy behould heere young man ſlew nephew sorbryn ſhall lead citie ſet ſure priſon ſhall ſhortly retourne againe fight againſt king iuoryn friend quoth galaffer require ſo doe aſſoone yee haue ſet priſon retourne againe gyant agrapart knew well entred citie would haue ſhewed thereof durſt vntill yee returned battaile pallaice pleaſeth neither man child liuing ſlaine except ſome xxx lady damſels ſhould wife put citie mine ill beſide ſhall helpe deſtroy frenchman citie anfalerne galaffer kneeled downe thanked king iuoryn courteſie ſhewed offered doe ſo would haue kiſſed foot iuoryn would ſuffer lift vp thus theſe vp gybet whereon hang minſtrell hath done great pleaſure would right ſorie ſhould haue ill gerames al companion made ready iſſued caſtle huon ſecret poſterne ſo gibet aware till huon companie among damoſell old man called gerames duke naymes bauyer heard gerard great maruaile ſayd gerames one ſayd ah deere god▪ heare great paine beleeue ſame gerames thinke companion together tourney holden brother demaunded beene holy sepulcher lord god hee ſaw demaunded ſore abaſhed ſo hee wiſt anſwere perceiued word hee beene sir demaunded hee furniſhed meſſage admirall gaudy hee could giue anſwere ſay word could beléeue ſaw could find truth word tooke ſet priſon howbeit full ſore againſt conſidered ſelfe muſt owe vnto grace faith fidelitie man man liuing though neuer ſo néere kinne yet would found treaſon therefore sir brother wife companion haue retained priſon wherefore sir doe herein ſhall pleaſe beſt prince lord vnderſtood word gerard taken brother huon put priſon none ſorry thereof many loue bare huon began wéepe demaunded gerard done déed ſaying ſurely done ſome manner treaſon chap lxx ¶ king commaunded huon ſhould ſent bourdeaux intent ſhould die emperour charlemaine vnderſtood gerard aroſe vp féet ſore troubled full yre gerardes wordes ancient hate diſpleaſure king huon death charlot ſonne renewed heart ſaid openly euery man might heare lordes héere preſent ſummon pledge huon ſuch wiſe traitour huon rendred hand doe pleaſure ſhall cauſe thē hanged drawne man court may ſo hardy ſpeake deſire contrarie ſhall cauſe die ſhamefull death thus ſaid ſate downe againe called duke naymes ſaid sir duke ye haue heard gerard hath ſayd brother huon sir quoth duke haue well heard beléeue matter otherwiſe hee hath ſayd man ſay contrarie gerard hath ſayd done falſe treaſon ſhall finde ſo matter wiſely enquired sir quoth gerard may ſay pleaſeth take god witneſſe father law gibouars good notable religious abbot chaplaine haue ſayd true would thing ſay iuſt true gibouars abbot chaplaine anſwered ſaid true gerard ſayd faith quoth duke naymes foure falſe lyars theeues king ill counſelled beléeue naymes quoth king pray ſeemeth vnto matter betwéen two brother sir quoth duke great matter accuſer brother hath ſet priſon come accuſeth becauſe hee knoweth well cannot come hither defend himſelfe ſhould great euil déed brother baniſhed france hee came mee refuge take ſet faſt priſon mine owne houſe goe complaine vpon intent purchaſe death ſay neuer noble man would thinke ſo doe haue done thus falſe traytours noble men ought beléeue ſuch ſpecially purchaſe ſuch deede againſt owne brother know well al haue imagined done falſe treaſon therfore ſay according right foure falſe traytours iudge part worthie receiue villanous death foure falſe witneſſes gerard heard duke naymes changed colour waxed white ſnow repenting himſelfe déede done brother hee curſed himſelfe gybouars hee beleeued counſell yet hee anſwered duke naymes ſayd ah sir ye doe great ill owe ill gerard quoth duke ilneſſe ye would one peeres france certainly ſuch councellor bée king hath litle néede rather haue loſt one hand ſhould haue conſented thereto duke naymes quoth king cauſe come ſuch pledge huon departing duke cauſed appeare ye king preſence diuers duke earles king charlemaine ſayd sir ye know well yee bee pledge huon bourdeaux know paine laide heades huon accompliſh meſſage gaue charge hee hath fulfilled wherefore without deliuer huon handes yee ſhall eſcape ye ſhall die sir quoth duke naymes god ſake require beleeue time counſell take good number notable men ſend bourdeaux let take huon priſon bring heare hee himſelfe ſay true gerard hath ſayd deſire haue pittie beléeue ſurely yee ſhall finde matter otherwiſe gerard brother hath ſayd naymes quoth king ſaying reaſonable accord thereto ſent chap lxxi ¶ emperor charlemain went himſelfe bourdeaux cauſe huon bee ſlaine great ill bare ye haue heard good duke naymes ſo much king charlemain content ſend huon king ſore diſpleaſed hée would abide ſo long ſend made himſelf readie go thether perſon traine commanded pledge ſhould ſet priſon till returne good duke naymes became pledge bée forth comming ſo went priſon king made readie tooke twelue péeres ſo tooke way towards bourdeaux god aide huon hee perill life god pitie thus haue ſhewed king charlemaine nobly accompanied rode ſo long iourneyes hee came within ſight bourdeaux approched neere citie gerard came king ſaid sir pleaſe would gladly ride citie ordain receiue accordingly gerard quoth king néede goe prepare comming ſhall goe ſhall goe till goe ſelfe duke naymes heard king anſwere hee ſaid king sir haue anſwered like noble prince bleſſed counſelled ſo ſay thus king rode forth without giuing knowledge comming ſo entered citie bourdeaux rode pallaice alighted dinner made readie king ſate duke naymes bordes lord knight richly ſerued great brute made pallaice ſo huon priſon great maruel noyſe heard demaunded gailer noyſe hee heard aboue pallaice gayler anſwered great pride deſpight ſayd néedes demaund like know ſoone ſince would know ſhall ſhew truth king charlemaine baron come hether iudge hanged goe thy way falſe traitour ah good lord quoth charlemaine haue great maruaile dwarfe may ſo rudly hath ſhouldred almoſt ouerthrowne table fierce hee thinkes ſcorne ſpeake howbeit ſee hee doe cannot tell hee thinketh doe ſeemeth refuſe ſoone hand drie voyde drop wine therin fellow quoth king haue inchaunted sir quoth oberon becauſe full ſin cup ſuch dignitie none drinke thereof without noble man cleane without deadly ſinne charlemaine art emperour romaine behold huon wrongfully without cauſe haue diſenherite would take land hee noble man true beſides ſay vnto truth hee hath done meſſage vnto admirall gaudy ayded bring death hée tooke mouth foure greateſt téeth alſo cutte white beard • loſe within ſide gerames god haue ſayd may bee ſurely beléeue theſe déedes preſent sée yonder falſe traitour gerard malicious intent hath done treaſon ende may know matter ſurely ſhall heare confeſſed owne mouth oberon ſayd gerard coniure thée diuine puiſſance power god hath giuen mee héere king charlemaine lord thou ſhew declare ye troth treaſon thou haſt done againſt huon thy brother gerard vnderſtoode oberon hee ſuch feare hée trembled dread hée felt himſelfe hee coulde haue power hide troth treaſon ſayd sir ſée well hide rheine hee taried two dayes refreſh vpon third day armed himſelfe called companie ſaid sir take leaue none ſhall goe nothing abaſhed hée alwayes hath ſaued mee peril forſake mee time hiſ men heard great maruaile would take voyage alone hee ſaide vnto sir haue doubt ſhall die vntill mine houre come coleyne enquired nothing eſtate warre beléeued would goe tourney lord ſaw would thus depart ſorrie perilous buſineſſe ſhould come mee ſhould aided king oberon needed haue ſaid ſo kinge oberon departed hee truſt vpon ayd therefore huon foole ill aduiſed truſt thereon vndertake ſo perilous enterprize great battaile within two league coleyn emperor almaine huon bourdeaux truce taken betweene h ʋon roade baron deuiſing old gerames regarded right hand towards ye litle wood ſaw wood great cleareneſſe many earth ſhall bee couered dead body enemy huon ordered battaile prouoſt coleyne comforted men ſaying sir emperour diſcomfited huon companie yonder abiding v thinke depart ſauegard haue power doe ſo
