brunt ſo many ſlaine whole fielde couered dead maimed men ſome ouerthrowne without hurt yet could neuer riſe becauſe great preaſe horſes runne ouer huon full ire becauſe hee thought vnder colour truce aſſayled ranne fiercely knight doone verie great hurt among men went coleyne ſuccour huon ſtrake cleane body speare ſo fell downe dead earth huon cryed crie call men together hée layd right ſide left ſo hee cutte armes legges raced helmet heades ſéemed rather man fayrie mortall man much doe men fought day ſore trauayled wearie howbeit defended ſelues right valiantly ſlew ſo many common coleyn bloud ran ground great ſtreames emperour iſſued wood lyttour came field heard brute crie battaile wherewith ſo abaſhed demaunded noiſe might sir quoth knight good prouoſt coleyn hath brought common citie coleyn aid ſuccour sir quoth emperour ſhall dearely buy howbeit thinke hee knoweth truce haue taken huon knew aduertiſed therof ſhould cauſe die il death goe command incontinent goe huon make amendes treſpaſſe doe charge incontinently ſlay emperour giuen commaundement one knight rode faſt might ye prouoſt right ſorrowfull loſt foure thouſand common knight ſlain came emperours knight ſayd sir prouoſt ye haue doone right ill ſéeing ye haue broken truce made betwéene huon emperour may gette yée ſhall neuer ſée fayre day without incontinent ye goe huon deale ſo content ſo reproch layd emperor prouoſt companie heard emperor commandement ſore abaſhed reculed back proueſt great feare hee done deſiring accompliſh emperours commandement ſtrake horſe ſpurres reſted till hrd found duke huon lighted foote tooke ſword ſayd ah right noble vertuous prince deſire thée honour ieſus chriſt haue pitie pardon iniurie haue done againſt haue done without knowledge licence emperour cauſe mee die ſhamefull death without yee pardon mee knew truce betwéene emperour thought beene dead sir haue done intent reſcue rightfull lord thereby haue loſt day foure thouſand burgeſſes common citie coleyn moſt part beſt friend therfore sir pray haue pittie elſe emperour ſlay mee ſette perpetuall pryſon chap lxxxvi ¶ huon arriued bourdeaux counſell fayre eſcleremond wife would beleeue follow huon vnderſtood prouoſt great pitie though ought reaſon pardon ſéeing hee done iuſt cauſe hee aduertiſed truce taken betweene emperour huon approched prouoſt ſayd friend ariſe vp pardon treſpaſſe haue done lord reaſonable ſince ye knew nothing truce ye haue done true ſubiect ought doe lord cannot bee angry ſame prouoſt tooke leaue huon returned emperour néere coleyn huon rode forth towards bourdeaux ſo wedneſday dinner entred bourdeaux wheras receiued great ſolemnitie bourgeſſes clergie citie alighted pallaice wheras ducheſſe eſcleremod wel receiued great ioy ſhe demaunded hee well good eſtate fayre lady quoth huon thanked bee lord god good health sir quoth ſhee comming right ioyous deſire ſhew aduentures madam quoth huon know truth haue béene mayens whereas found emperour duke raoull nephew proclaimed tourney becauſe aduertiſed comming intention found hee concluded men haue ſlaine mee grace god haue done ſo much preſence emperour vncle preſent ſtrake head becauſe made auaunt ſoone ſlaine would haue wife mine heritage ſlaine departed haſte mayens long emperour followed men mounted vpon good horſe yee haue ſéene ſo good beléeue ſurely ſuch another world emperour great deſire reuenge death nephew duke raoull vaunced himſelfe bow ſhoote companie cryed many iniurious word ſaw farre men turned toward ranne bare earth tooke good horſe mounted let mine owne go wh • n men ſawe lying earth feared leſt beene dead aſſembled tooke héede follow mee becauſe knew well folly follow ſéeing mounted emperor good horſe thus departed went lay night coleyne whereas found men left went emperours court alone next day departed gone farre coleyn emperour tenne thouſand men mette way whereas lien little wood waite ranne men great battaile part many ſlain wounded ſo much grace god good company ouercame ſlew two nephew bare emperour earth ſaw loſſe battaile ranne ſide ſent mee meſſenger haue truce halfe yeere granted becauſe thought doone diſpleaſure inough ſlaying thrée nephewes thus departed returned met prouoſt coleyn brought twentie thouſand men haue reſcued emperour ſo fought together ſoone emperour aduertiſed thereof hee ſent commaunded ſhould fight mee prouoſt came cryed mercie done excuſing himſelfe knew nothing truce wee made ſound retrayt part thus wee departed without ſtrokes giuing whereof thanke god thus ſcaped sir quoth eſcleremond ye ought thanke god hee hath ſent grace haue heard ſay emperour haue ſlain two nephewes great puiſſant rich prince right ſage expert war wherefore feared lette matter thus reſt madam quoth huon know well ſay true thinke well diſpleaſed mee death nephewes many kin thus haue ſaid iuſted two time ſecond time ſtrake earth ſuch wiſe hee brake thigh ſo hee conſtrained bee borne thence litter hath beene told ſince loſſe good horſe gréeueth loſſe men lady ſhew peril aduentures haue ſince departed would long ſhew ſurely thinke ſoone truce expired emperour puiſſance wil come beſiege bourdeaux hath béene ſhewed troth emperour hath ſo made oath promiſe hath ſworne crowne imperiall depart hence till haue taken deſtroyed citie sir quoth eſcleremond beleeue ye ſhall reſiſt ſhall tell ye know well haue brother called king salybraunt king bougye extendeth one ſide néere mombraunt ſide néere trypoley barbary may leade battaile hundred thouſand men sir ſurely hee good chriſtian howbeit know verily hath beleeued ieſus chriſt sir goe deſire aide ſame token priſoner babylon diſcouered ſecrets minde ſhewed loue betwéene ye would leade fraunce whereof hee ioyfull deſired affectuouſly ſhould doe ſo much might come ſee realme aduenture fell ſo departing fell otherwiſe deuiſed ſaw howe father ſlaine ſuch feare ranne away hide garden behinde pallayce tarried till night ſtole away went owne realme ſhall yee finde goe thither know ſurely hee make excéeding great good chéere refuſe ayde ſuccour hée bee ſo excéeding puiſſaunt mightie hee bring hundred thouſand sarizens alſo sir would counſaile aduiſe take along wyth ſome fiue ſixe prieſtes well furniſhed wyth oyle creame aſſoone hee hath men owne countrey hee cauſe chriſtened ſuch cauſe die ill death sir require beleeue counſaile time knowe well fraunce ſhall get ſuccor ſome would yet dare doubt king charlemaine hate hath yet quenched death ſonne charlot neuer forget sir yée goe brother ſuccour yée may happen repent peraduenture may late doe doth ſhutteth ſtable dore horſe ſtollen thus faire ladie eſcleremond exhorted duke huon huſband whome ſhée loued entierly chap lxxxvii ¶ huon great ioy birth claryet daughter huon well heard wife hée ſaid right deare ladie companion right well know great loue beare mee hath conſtrayned ſay thus whereof thanke lord vpon croſſe died redeeme humane lineage goe place ſend ſuccours vntill ſée citie haue cauſe labour ſuccours vntill feele ſtroaks almaines bauiers giue owne countrey longe ſheeld hole found firſt thinke ſhall feele ſharpneſſe speares head good sword yet god grace ſhall abandon leaue city good burgeſſes might greatly bée layd reproach ſhould thus goe away ala sir quoth eſcleremond yée may well know haue ſaid feare haue haue béene well aduertiſed emperour ſore hateth without cauſe nephewes lord yée haue ſlaine therefore sir ye beléeue yée ſhall haue men defend brought hether king brother ſo emperour come land ſhall lie either make peace warre reaſon made ſome amends hurt yée haue done vnto part haue peace thē ſhall lie make ſuch warre ſo ſhall depart without agréement great loſſe sir feare haue looſe conſtrayneth thus ſay haue heard often time ſaid entrie warre large iſſuing therof ſtraight warre cauſeth pouertie ſéeing pleaſure beléeue reaſon muſt content pleaſure ſhalbe fulfilled entred deuiſes great ioy feaſts made pallaice bourdeaux huon lordes countrey laſt faire ladie eſcleremond great child fell vpon trauayling ſhée prayed god helpe ſuffered great paine whereof huon great pitie whē heard thereof loue betwéene excéeding great laſt lady brought bed faire daughter whereof huon thanked god entred lady chamber great number lady fairie came eſcleremonds bedſide ſaid ladie yée ought 〈◊〉 thanke god yée haue brought foorth faireſt beſt creature world whome lord god hath graunted moſt grace birth faire deſt wiſe courteous hath béen borne c yéeres paſt ſhée ſhall haue ſuch deſtinie fortune world realme aragon ſhée ſhall bee crowned quéene ſhée ſhall ſo gouerne ſelfe ſhée ſhalbe accounted ſhe saint paradice tortouſe church ſhe honoured founded name named saint clare eſcleremond ioyfull wordes theſe lady fairie great ioy feaſting made euery birth child greatly regarded lady fayrie ſaid child faireſt creature world tooke child bleſſed thrée time layd downe departed ſuddainly ſo man wiſt become whereof lady great maruaile tidings brought vnto huon right ioyfull ſayd worthy king oberon beleeue ſurely yet haue forgotten doubt nothing emperour puiſſance ſéeing haue remembraunce mee huon came hall thether daughter brought vnto ſée hée tooke armes ſhewed lord ioyfull ſée ſhee borne church great ſolemnitie chriſtened named clariet bicauſe ſhe ſo faire cleare behold ſhee brought ducheſſe great ioy ducheſſe kept chamber moneth ſhe churched whereof court ioyfull ſuch feaſting made ſhould ſhewe rich nobleneſſe ſhewed ſhould ouerlong rehearſe therefore wil leaue ſpeaking thereof time vntill another ſeaſon chap lxxxviii ¶ emperour aſſembled great hoaſt came vnto bourdeaux ye haue large heard manner cauſe war mooued betweene emperour almaine huon duke bourdeaux truce expired emperour hole thigh huon broken publiſhed war againe ſent ouer empire euerie duke earle baron knight squier ſhould come souldiers part within moneth citie mayence entent make warre vppon huon bourdeaux commaundement publiſhed ſuch diligence made day appointed euerie man come city mayence lodged citie pauilions citie aſſembled fortie thouſand men well appointed warre emperour named tirrey ſaw verie ioyfull ſore threatned huon made promiſe baron hee would neuer returne owne countrey vntill hee firſt ſlaine huon hadde doone ſo great damage hee commaunded conſtables marſhals readie depart next day take way towardes coleyne artilerie carriage done next day emperour entred feeld ſo road towards coleyne emperor within league met old sauarie brother father duke raoul ſlaine huon theſe two brother met together great ioy made betwéene duke sauary beganne wéepe ſayd brother emperour sir comming right ioyfull pitious death deare beloued ſonne nephew raoull commeth minde member dolour diſpleaſure trembleth neuer haue perfect ioye heart long hath done mee diſpleaſure liueth duke sauary noble man betwéene ſonne raoull great difference duke raoull vntrueſt traitor euer liued wickednes procéeded ducheſſe mother daughter hurdowin fraunce moſt vntrueſt falſeſt traytour liued world emperour heard brother ſpeake teares fell eye embraced ſayd right deare brother dolour much diſpleaſeth mee dolour mine thereof haue part ye haue much ioy part ſhall likewiſe therein poſſible v haue againe make ſorrow god ayde huon frō enemy greatly deſire death yet oftentimes deſire another man death auaunceth thus haue heard emperour duke sauary entred citie coleyne whereas receiued great ioy ſo rode pallayce ſupped make long rehearſall good chéere made supper went reſt next morning roſe heard ſeruice tooke ſop wine departed coleyne goodly hoaſt behold carriage artillerie reached foure league length thus ſworne death huon paſſed high borgoyn dolphinne ſo paſſed riuer roan ſo countrey bourdeaux leaue ſpeaking till another ſeaſon chap lxxxix ¶ euery man readie armes come bourdeaux becauſe aduertiſed comming en • mies meſſengers made ſuch diligence within fifteene dayes euerie man come bourdeaux duke huon receiued great ioy repayred citie towres walles well furniſhed victual artillerie ſuch caſe well appertained time citie bourdeaux ſo ſtrong duke huon ſaw citie ſo well garniſhed men victuales right ioyfull called old gerames ſayd right deere friend ye ſee wel warre apparent betweene emperour mee wel aduertiſed comming ready come 〈◊〉 beſiege citie therefore heartie deere friend▪ hath ayded ſo many buſineſſes pray counſell ayde conduct warre ye haue charge comfort men well ſo v euill report • e enemy haue cauſe prayſe warre haue againſt v bee returned country make auaunts among wenthes louers sir quoth gerames thanke honour great truſt haue mee howbeit ye haue many ſage hardie great charge ſhould better appertaine syr ſhall ſo acquite truſt ſhall reprehended thus haue heard huon made deuiſes among baron made ordinance defence citie manner iſſuing appoynted men reſcue reculing emperour entred countrey bourdeaux mightie armie burning deſtroying countrey whereof poore people ſore abaſhed becauſe neuer war thus emperour neuer reſted waſting deſtroying countrey till came cittie bourdeaux hee pitcht vp tent pauillions emperour lay way leading paris part duke sauary father raoull lodged emperours marſhalles ſo cittie cloſed round huon within cittie beheld countenaunces manner lodging commaunded men ſhould readie iſſue vpon enemy huon armed himſelfe verie richly mounted vpon good horſe emperours ſware ere returned would ſhew enemy bourdeaux could doe hee mounted good horſe hee came citie found old gerames readie apparelled companie appoynted fiue thouſand men keepe citie twentie thouſand men goe thus v déerely ye haue heard departed ſéeke ſuccour cannot tell part hee gone realme fraunce know right well hee ſhall haue ſuccour hath béene ſhewed mée • ate right noble victorious prince charlemaine dead loued huon little becauſe ſonne charlot whome huon ſlew charlemaine hath left behinde one ſonne named lewes yong age beléeue hee full age would rather come ſuccour huon ſlewe charlot brother therfore otherwiſe gone ſome far countrey ſuccour therefore thinke beſt meane time ere returne ſides let v continually aſſaile citie let euerie one doe part bee reuenged death friendes héere ſlaine part thoſe iſſued taken ſlaine ah good lord loſſe fell citie bourdeaux ah noble lady eſcleremond yee may well weepe complaine dayes ſorow paine dolour approacheth néere whereby ye like beare ſuch diſeaſes pouertie man liuing recount yee ſhall neuer bee daunger trouble till yee deliuered good duke huon huſband gerames companie readie mounted horſes iſſued gate priuily could ſo perceiued ſet watch heard field rode falſe gallop tent might well • e cleerely light tent came neere daſhed ſpurres horſes cryed bourdeaux ſ • rake cut aſunder cordes ſtayes ſo many tent fell earth ſuch came ſlaine great noyſe crie beganne riſe hoaſt euerie man ranne armour gerames companie ſlew many enemy made flie dreadfull beholde damage finally loſſe fell vpon emperour men readie gerames ſawe howe hoaſt mooued ſayd companie sir time v retyre backe may tarrie héere long yonder commeth emperour mightie armie cloſe v needfull v make haſte wee may goe away ſafetie altogether one companie returned went way towards bourdeaux gone farre ere ouertaken almaynes layd part ſwords ſpeares gerames turned almaine ſpeare ran cleane drawing ſpeare hee fell downe dead earth ſtrake another whome alſo ſlew ſuch déedes armes ere ſpeare brake hee ſlewe fiue enemy whereof almaynes ſore abaſhed brake preaſe ſuch wiſe none durſt approach néere vnto right well othon bernard ſuch duke sauary tenne thouſand men lay taken ſlaine earneſtly called vpon lord ieſus chriſt requiring ſaue defend good lord huon bourdeaux ducheſſe eſcleremond wife cryed companie ſayd sir pray hartily time ſhew forth proweſſe behaue ſelues ſo valiantly emperour almaines haue cauſe make auaunts haue found v men amazed let v ſhew ſwords cut together aſſayled enemy ſuch wiſe ye firſt brunt almaines conſtrayned retyre backe gerames ſuch déeds none durſt approach néere vnto duke sauary ten thouſand men came vpon ſodainely equall part alſo emperour great battaile came alſo vpon old gerames companie gotten themſelues ſubburbs citie mightie wall behind theyr backes whereas ſtand bay againſt almaines gerames middeſt vnderneath helmet appeared long white beard emperour great ſhame ſo men number ſhould kéepe baye againſt highneſſe doe vnto men ſo great damage perceiued old gerames oftentimes ſlaine many men done ſo mightie damage hee thought hee could neuer reuenged thereof ſufficiently thought hee ſhould haue ſcaped aliue hee would doe much hurt damage ſayd himſelfe hee rather die incontinent ſhould bee reuenged therewith incontinent couched speare ran old gerames one ſide ere aware ſo emperour ranne cleane bodie ſo gentle knight gerames fell earth died incontinent great damage fell day huon bourdeaux loſt trueſt beſt friend ala pitious iourney fell day bourdeaux good cauſe wéepe ala good ducheſſe eſcleremond loſſe haue yee receiued looſe cheefe comfort refuge ye might haue called father ah right noble ladie neuer came greater miſchiefe ye haue death gerames lieth dead euen among enemy almaines ſawe gerames dead fought ſo within ſhort ſpace bourdeaux ſlaine one ſcaped aliue except barnard puiſſant horſe amphage gambaudes worke made almaine durſt approach neere bernard next vnto huon moſt valiaunt knight body liuing almaines ſawe vpon horſe chaſed went theyr tent bernard ceaſed till hee came vnto gate citie opened hee entred gate cloſed againe burgeſſes comunaltie ſaw bernard came alone demaunded ſayd sir captaine old gerames ſore wéeping ſhewed length pittious dolorous aduenture heard made ſuch cry wéeping pittie heare ſée bruite noyſe ſo great loud ladie eſcleremond heard whereat ſhe maruailed ſtood great feare therewith syr bernard entred caſtle gate ſo mounted hall whereas hee found ducheſſe eſcleremond ſore abaſhed ſhe ſawe syr bernard come alone ſhewed great loſſe ſuſtained day wherwith inward ſorrow ſhe fell ſwound ſo lay long ſpace though ſhe beene dead ladyes damſels ſore wéeping reléeued ſhee caſt great crie wringing handes tearing hayre ſayde ah huon right déere lord day yée haue loſt moſt ſorrowfull dolorous wife well beloued daughter lady damſelles wiues loſt huſbands father brother came caſtle made ſuch cryes ſorrow noyſe thereof heard emperours hoaſt without ſhewed emperour noyſe brute made within citie caſtle loſſe hadde receiued day ſayde ſhould good next morning euerie man ſhould readie goe aſſayle citie ſayd euer would winne howre come emperour heard reaſon ſayd aduiſe good would ſhould ſo done hee gaue charge thereof conſtable marſhalles ſo next morninge hoaſt readie emperour commanded ſet forward came citie garniſhed thing néedfull neceſſarie aſſault walles defended cittie citie ſo ſore aſſayled part defendant wiſt make reſiſtance ſhotte without ſlew ſo thicke none within durſt appeare vppon walles whereby entred perforce citie ſlew many mette withall entring went vnto gate opened ſo emperour lord entred citie euerie man went abroade ſtréetes take priſoners ſpoyle men houſes emperour ſaw hee lord citie hee cauſed proclaimed euerie ſtreete man paine death ſhould wrong woman deflowre anie mayde breake church ſet houſe fire alſo ſuch church ſauegard ſhould goe pleaſure without trouble danger either body good emperour wiſe prince thought himſelfe great damage pittie would bee deſtroy putte ruine ſuch famous citie ſo ſtrong well furniſhed burgeſſes marchants ſuch fledde ſtrong place refuge vnderſtood emperours commaundement euerie man woman returned owne houſes ſo little damage done done entred firſt lady eſcleremond ſaw citie taken ye may bee ſure ſhe right ſorrowfull firſt ſhee ſaw citie taken enemie ſelfe cloſed within caſtle ill furniſhed victualles much people whereby ſhe ſaw cleerely without god ayde death approched neere pitiouſly ſhe complayned god ſayd verie god whome beléeue firmely whoſe ſake haue left firſt miſbeleefe forſooke parent friend take huſband chriſtian man intēt receiue thy law god require thee thy grace haue pittie vpon mee poore deſolate creature keepe defend deere child ill incombrances thy pleaſure ſaue childe content abide fortune ſhall pleaſe thee ſend mee beſide require thy grace ſaue keepe huon deere lord huſband wéeping ſhe called vnto ſir bernard ſaid▪ right deare fréend take mine honour loue good lord maiſter huon woulde neuer depart hence reſiſtance force ſmall value becauſe woulde ſerue bounde doe readie ſourniſhed take vppon mee aduenture beare child away ſet ſauegard whereas found great ſtore plentie victual yee haue heard howe huon caſtle adamant great pouertie famine whereas beene tenne dayes without meat drinke except apple fruit grew garden whereby became ſo féeble weake ſcarre power ſuſtaine himſelfe vppon feete hee found rich inough gould ſiluer apparell iewels riche bedding ſo wanted nothing except victuall hee walked chamber whereas treaſure lay caſting downe lookes earth reaſon long mantle ſwept powder away pauement appeared letter gould written vpon pauement red tennour whoſoeuer read letter ſhall find vnder pauement celler victuall bread huon barnard oftentimes thanked god good aduenture ſent thus yée haue heard admirall perſia aſſembled great number people made readie entred ſhippe diuers shippes ſhipped armour horſes huon deſired pleaſe admirall tooke owne little shippe diſcharged tooke precious ſtones put another ſhip admirall deliuered ſerue ſayd vnto admirall sir know well little ſhip came hether ſerue warres therefore sir doe giue vnto whereof admirall great ioy world none ſuch beautie rich huon gaue admirall buſhell ſtones vnto lordes together thanked huon courteſie large ſtones kept owne vſe thrée hundred gaue away ought greatly thanke lord ieſus chriſt faire aduenture ſée v enemy chriſtian faith grace lord sauiour ieſus chriſt day ſhall doe ſo much citie inhabitant therein ſhall handes vſe pleaſure sir quoth admirall beſéech almightie god giue v grace may ſo great grace lord god ſhall doe vnto v wee may winne citie admirall cauſed men bee armed ſawe halfe league citie port hauen kept defended becauſe aduaunced forward number fiftie thouſand men theſe twoo hoaſtes ſawe none feared death day faire cleare ſo approached ruſh partes daſhed together ſuch wiſe reaſon pouder duſt riſe horſes sunne faire bright waxed darke • ſhot partes flewe ſo faſt thicke though ſnowed firſt méeting many ſpeares broken many knight borne earth ſo could neuer releeued lay ground among horſe feete died dolour many horſes running abroad trayling bridle maſters lying dead vppon earth bloud myre great ſlaughter made vppon part huon went breaking great preaſſes whereas hee ſlewe ſo many paynim euerie man feared ſaw ranne another gaue ſuch maruailous ſtroake paſſed ſheeld bodie drawing ſpeare hee fell earth neuer reléeued ſo thrée foure hee ſerued like manner ſo valiantly behaue himſelfe ſlewe eight speare brake drew sword therewith hee ſuch déedes fearfull behold hee cut legges armes raſſed helmet ſo none enemy durſt approach néere vnto fledde birde doth hauke hee brake aſunder thicke preaſſes hee ſo bee feared enemy left hee neuer ſtrooke man full ſtroake hee receiued ſlaine alſo barnard coozen euer followed maruailes armes hee ſharpe eager knight alſo admirall angory enforced himſelfe doe dammage vnto chriſtian men hée ſawe admirall perſia ſlaying men came ranne admirall perſia ſawe encountred ſuch force puiſſance bare earth quickly releeued themſelues sword hand willing ſlay beene done indéede men come ſuccoured thether came ſo many part twoo admiral hadde power one touch great force came thether paynim sarazins ſo chriſtian men could remount vp againe admirall perſia faine fight thether hope hée ſhall doe vnto v farre greater grace yet ayde v conquer deſtroy thoſe way beléeue holy lawe chéefeſt entent voyage thus deuiſed together ſpace eight dayes without finding aduenture ſo vppon euening huon alone ſtood leaning ouer ſhippe board beholding sea plaine peaceable hee remembred ducheſſe eſcleremond wife therewith teares ran tenderly downe viſage ſaid ah right noble ladie sir knowe well fortune aduentures haue come vnto god hath ayded ſaued perill death therefore take good comfort ſelfe laud praiſe lord god ſendeth vnto doubt haue perfect hope truſt ayd comfort neuer forgetteth good heart ſerue thus ſuch wordes barnard comforted huon admirall came leaned huon deuiſed together diuers ſundrie matter ſame time aroſe vp wind tempeſt ſo great ſo horrible ſayles broken diuers place ſome maſtes brake flew ouer board ſhippe ſea beganne bee rough furious ſo euerie man thought haue beene periſhed fortune tempeſt ſo horrible euerie man deuoutly called vpon lord god ſaue perill daunger sir quoth huon pray ſhewe mee countrey yonder ſee mée happie fortunate wee might arriue caſt anchor vnder rocke ſee sir quoth admirall wée bée arriued euill port wee bée néere deſerts feare admirall ſaid vnto marriners sir pray may bee let v drawe quarter sir quoth huon mee thinkes ſore diſmayed • aſh • lord made ſemblance ſhall neuer haue ioy heart vntill knowe enemie cauſeth periſh ſo faſt way ſhall neuer reſt vntill haue ſpoken hee doe thinge contrarie pleaſure ſhall ſtrike head huon quoth admirall haue great maruaile doe ſaye fiue hundred ſuch bée within one houre ſhould bée dead ſtangled sir quoth huon doubt though ſhould die quarrell goe ſée knowe cauſe hée letteth troubleth paſſage three dayes end ſhal goe ſpeake fortune ſoeuer commeth thereof sir quoth admirall doe owne ſince pleaſeth muſt bee content would beleeue mée ſhould take vpon voyage enterprize sir quoth huon ſmiling haue hope truſt almightie god hath heeretofore ſaued death ſo hope doe yet common prouerbe ſayd hee whome god ayde ſuccour man hurt sir quoth admirall pray vnto lord god defend euill giue grace returne againe ſauegard sir quoth huon thanke heartily barnard aroſe vp ſaide goe mee ſelfe ieſus chriſt bleſſed mother whoſe ſauegard commit ſelfe barnard heard hee great ſorrowe heart ſo admirall ſawe could turne huon dangerous voyage enterprize huon armed himſelfe tooke great sea whereof admirall barnard lordes great feare greatly complained huon alone without companie mounted vppon mountaine hee going hee looked downe sea ſawe maruailous tempeſt sea ſo two hundred ſhips hee left admirall could ſée two together al reſt ſeperated one another great perill danger hée began pitifully wéepe complayne wife faire eſcleremond whome thought neuer ſée becauſe hee deſert ſawe ſhippes driuen land great feare looſing kneeled downe held vp handes vnto heauen requiring lord god pitie grace ayd giue comfort hee might eſcape thence aliue ſaue ſhippes bring againe ſauegard place whence departed gréeuouſly complained wife daughter ſayde ah right noble ladie eſcleremond remember paine dolor pouerties cauſe ſuffer haue ſuffered body ſweateth paine dolour ala thought ſhort ſpace haue aided ſuccoured nowe ſée well departing come euer yonder perilous sea ſée coozen barnard diuers lord cauſe way perdition without god doe ayd ſuccour whome humbly require ſend grace may arriue ſome good port may ſée againe entent may fight againſt paynim sarazins exalting law ieſus chriſt thus huon bourdeaux made prayer lord ieſus chriſt chap cxx ¶ huon went ſo long deſert found cain ſpake long ſeaſon hee beguiled cain departed huon hadde thus made prayer vnto lord god aroſe vp bleſſed ſigne croſſe recommending himſelfe vnto lord god came toppe mountaine hée bodie trembled trauaile ſo verie faint féeble hée looked round ſawe faire meadowe cleare fountaine thether went refreſh reſt layde downe vppon graſſe refreſh hee would drinke ſo hot well cooled hée came fountaine dranke thereof little waſhed hand face went forreſt could find neither towne caſtle garden trées fruit whereof hée right ſorrowfull ſore diſpleaſed ſo ſearched day find ſome man woman al vaine ſawe sunne went reſt could find creature ſore diſcomforted choſe trée vnder layd downe ſlept morning ſaw sunne riſe beames ſpread abroad vppon earth aroſe bleſſed ſo went foorth deſert found neither man woman beaſt birde wherewith ſorrowfull angrie deuoutly hée called vppon lord god praying haue tuition kéeping bodie ſoule might yet ſée wife faire eſcleremond clariet daughter went ſo long deſert laſt came plain thrée bowe ſhoot large middeſt thereof ſawe tunne made heart oake bound band yron turned rowled playne neuer paſſed circuit plaine beſide tunne ſaw lay vppon ground great mall yron great maruaile huon hée ſawe tunne roule thus without ceaſe like tempeſt paſſed huon hee heard pitifull voice within tunne ſore complaning hee heard two thrée time hée approached néere tunne ſayd thou art tunne ſpeake vnto mée ſhewe mée thou art thing thou haſt néede thou art put tunne heard huon reſted ſtill ſpake word huon ſaw would ſpeake ſayd whatſoeuer thou art coniure thée created world sonne lord ieſus chriſt ſent downe ſuffer death paſſion vppon trée croſſe redéeme fréends ſinne adam eue limbo glorious reſurrection angel archangel cherubins seraphins holy saint coniure thée ſhewe mee thou art cauſe thou art ſet heere tunne hee within tunne heard howe ſore hee coniured anſweared ſaid thou haſt coniured mée thou doeſt great euill cauſe ſhew thée troth know ſurely haue name cain sonne vnto adam eue hee ſlewe brother abell falſe curſed enuie vnto becauſe oblation diſmes made vnto god exalted fume thereof went vpward heauen thoſe made fume went downeward ſawe ſlewe murdered brother abell wherefore great ſinne haue committed damned bee ſuffer martirdome within tunne wherein cloſed burning serpent toad héere within deuouring mee yet cannot die héere ſhall bee vntill day iudgement paine ſhall doubled haue ſhewed thee thy demaund wherefore repute thée foole thou art ſo hardy enter deſert whereas neuer man entred departed without death know troth hether repaireth twoo enemy féends hell ſhall ſlay thée beare thy ſoule hell without thou wilt doe ſhall ſhew thée fréend quoth huon pray thee ſhew thou ſpeakeſt thing thou wilt ſhould doe doe entent may depart hence nothing world ſhall doe thée ſo thou wilt ſhewe mée way howe may depart hence fréend quoth cain ſhall ſhewe thée thou ſhalt doe thou ſhalt take mall iron thou ſéeſt ſtrike therewith ſo long vppon tunne vntill thou haſt broken entent may yſſue deliuered ſhall ſet thée ſauegard ieruſalem france countrey ſoeuer thou wilt wiſh thou wilt doe haue ſayd deliuer torment ſhall ſet thée whereſoeuer thou wilt land chriſtian heathen thou doeſt haue ſaide night ſhall cauſe thée die great tormentes anon thou ſhalt ſée come hether two diuels hell foule hideous behold ſhall ſtangle thée beare thy ſoule hell ah good lorde quoth huon humbly require beſeech thée ſaue mée torment cain quoth huon thou ſpeakeſt mée faire ſayeſt thou liſt deliuer thée tunne vntill firſt thou ſheweſt mée may depart hence cain ſayd thou wilt promiſe mée thy faith thy part paradice deliuer mée tunne ſhall ſhewe thée manner howe thou ſhalt eſcape hence cain quoth huon haue doubt promiſe thée kéepe faith ſo thou wilt ſhew mee manner howe may depart deſert ſhall deliuer thée thy torment cain ſaid thou ſhalt goe little path thou ſéeſt héere vppon thy right hand ſhall bring thée ſtraight seaſide farre hence goe downe mountaine whereas thou ſhalt find ſhippe therein one man thou doeſt enter ſhippe bleſſe thrée time hée thou ſhalt finde féende hell ſhewe vnto howe thou art cain eſcaped rowling tun bid paſſe thée ouer ſay thou wilt goe ſlay chriſtian men bee world bring ſoules hell hée heareth thée ſay thus hee wlil paſſe thée ouer ſafetie longe ſince hee hath taried mee becauſe thinketh ſhould eſcape tun thou muſt take thée mall yron vpon thy necke entent hee ſhall better beleeue thee ſurely paſſe thee ouer cain quoth huon pray thee troth thou haſt ſayd fréend quoth cain lye neuer word pray thée ſeeing haue ſhewed thée manner thou mayeſt eſcape take mall yron breake aſunder tunne may deliuered paine torment cain quoth huon pray thee ſhew mee hee put thée tun name sir quoth cain know troth god heauen ſet héere becauſe diſpleaſed ſlaying brother abell wherefore haue ſuffered ſo much paine ſorow cannot endure therefore yet againe pray thee deliuer mee hence cain quoth huon god forbid ſhould deliuer thee ſéeing lord god hath ſet thee know troth thou ſhalt neuer depart thence except bee commaundement thou ſhalt bee euer mee rather bee periured vndoe thing god haue done puniſh thee euils thou haſt done knowe well euill haue done breaking promiſe thee god lightly pardon mee abide thou thy curſed ſinnes ſure mee thou ſhalt haue none ayd chap cxxi ¶ huon departed cain paſſed sea ʋeſſell guided diuell beleeued beene cain huon arriued citie called colander whereas found admirall perſia barnard cozen layde ſiege citie cain well vnderſtood huon ſaid ah thou falſe traytor beguiled mocked thou art worthy beleeued thinge thou ſayeſt thou lyeſt worſe dogge oh thou falſe periured traitour thou haſt ill kept thy promiſe thou art worthy bee beleeued cain quoth huon good getteſt thou none mee thou art worthie bee heard thou haſt ſtaine thy deare brother falſe enuie curſed treaſon whereof thou art full goe thy way falſe traytour much euill cannot bée done vnto thee bee content tunne thou art thou néedeſt feare refreſhing furthering mee well haſt thou deſerued within ſhort time thou ſhalt haue worſe paine ſorrow ah traytour quoth cain falſe lyer thou haſt loſt thy part paradice thou lyeſt quoth huon vnto thee ought bee kept neither faith promiſe becauſe thou haſt ſlaine abell thy brother wherefore thou art puniſhed well haſt thou deſerued ah thou falſe lier quoth cain ſubtilly thou haſt deceiued mocked mee thy falſe word ſubtilties ſee well thou wilt goe hence leaue ſtill paine certainly quoth huon promiſed thee beguile thee mee thou ſhalt come without hee commaund ſet thee heere well huon quoth cain know certaine thy life thou wert neuer better counſailed thou haddeſt deliuered incontinent would haue ſtrangled thee ah falſe feend quoth huon yet haſt thou repentaunce thine euill thou haſt done goe way thou ſhalt abide heere ſtill great pain torment foreuer therewith huon departed tooke mall vppon necke entred little way cain ſhewed vnto leaue ſpeaking huon ſpeake within ſo hideous horrible behold maruaile ſee hee ſéemed well bee diuell hell head great oxe head eye • edder two burning coales téeth great long rough beare hee caſt fire ſmoake gorge like furnace maruaile though huon doubted hee ſawe ſo foule hee great feare ſo lent himſelfe rocke better behold hee bleſſed ſigne croſſe recommending himſelfe ſauegard lord god fortuned ſo ſame time enemie ſawe ah good lord quoth huon pray require thee humbly counſaile mee manner ſhould truſt foule féend fearfull ſo behold maruaile might bee acquainted whether might truſt ſhippe certainly haue great doubt hee caſt sea elſe ſlay mee ſide sea wotte doe muſt bee faine truſt elſe returne deſert whereas ſhall die famine neuer ſée wife child ſéeing thus ſhall aduenture ſelfe may eſcape aduenture ſhall goe holy sepulchre whereas lorde ieſus chriſt quicke dead ſhall make warre vpon sarazins duke huon tooke vppon heart courage mall vppon necke hee marched foorth fiercely hee called enemy ſaid oh thou kéepeſt veſſell paſſage paſſe incontinent ouer sea ſet land vpon ſide diuell ſawe huon mall vppon necke ſpeaking ſo fiercely hee ſaid art thou whether wilt thou goe doeſt thou ſeeke héere art thou ſo bold come hether thou ſhalt neuer goe ſhall caſt thee sea ſtrangle thée beare thy soule hell huon heard beganne tremble nothing abaſhed hadde fainted taried haue made anſweare hee incontinent béene deſtroyed ſlaine like hardy knight full great proweſſe firme faith ieſus chriſt ſayde hold thy peace thou foole cain whome thou haſt taried héere ſo long came euen rowling tunne vpon mountaine haſt thée paſſe mée ouer arme sea ſhall find neither man woman beléeueth ieſus chriſt ſhall ſlay entent hell may filled ſoules féend heard huon ſay ſo great ioy ſaid cain haſt thou made tarie héere ſo long haue ioyfull thy comming could neuer haue departed place without thou haddeſt béen deliuered tunne therefore cain come thy way enter ship preſently ſhall bring thée whereas thou wilt gladly paſſe thée ouer sea entent thou ſhouldeſt ſlay chriſtian men sarazins haue soules hell huon entred ship recommending himſelfe lord ieſus chriſt ſayde quickly paſſe ouer huon thought gone two league ouer ſide whereof huon great maruaile hee ſo ſoone ouer thanked lord god hee daunger hee tooke leaue enemie ſayde farewell returne againe ſhortly within theſe thrée dayes thou ſhalt heare tidinges mee féend anſweared ſhortly ſayd cain goe thy way quickly haſt thée entent thou returneſt hell thou ſhalt haue good chéere maiſters greatly deſire thy comming huon departed quickly thought euer diuell followed hee went ſo longe hee approached citie called colander glad huon hee loſt ſight euill spirit euening entred citie colander mall vppon necke paynim sarazins within citie great maruaile came alone afoote cleane armed citie among one demaunded hee hee went ſo alone armed huon anſwered fiercely abaſh therewith ſaid cain mine ilneſſe ſlew abell brother wherewith god angrie mée bee longe time ſhall take ſuch vengeance many men woman child find beléeuing lawe ieſus chriſt ſhall deſtroy ſuch wiſe paynim sarazins ſhall haue doubt euill ſhall doe vnto ſhall deſtroy ſlay neither ſparing old young paynim heard right ioyfull night ſerued huon well made great feaſt becauſe truſted hee ſhould deſtroy chriſtendome ſaide among themſelues hee welcome thether becauſe citie day beſieged admirall perſia thus huon great ioy feaſting made vnto supper brought faire rich chamber wherein hee lay ſlept ſoundly vntill next morning chap cxxii ¶ huon bourdeaux great ioy ſawe admirall perſia colander fought sarazins admirall perſia left huon deſert abillaunt great ſtorme vppon ſea laſt shippes aſſembled together arriued port citie colander citie huon right ioyfull knew admirall come thether lay ſiege citie admirall companie ſorrowfull becauſe loſt huon eſpecially barnard coozen thought neuer haue ſeene againe hee ſhortly tidinges yée ſhall heare admirall arriued port armed themſelues ordained men well might aſſayle citie colander yſſued shippes came marching towards city made great aſſault paynim sarazins armed ſides went defence captaine towne came vnto huon ſaid come foorth cain time ſhew doe héere without chriſtian men aſſayling citie pray ſpare wee haue great truſt sir quoth huon ſéeing citie yée néede feare perſon anon yée ſhall ſée doe cain quoth captaine pray goe wee ſhall followe well quoth huon mall ſhall aſtone paynim great ioy word wéening ſurely cain huon armed himſelfe hee good horſe brought vnto whereuppon hee mounted paynim yſſued citie found admirall perſia companie readie arriued battaile hee ſawe sarazins yſſued hee ſette vppon fiercely huon ioyfull aduenture fallen hee ſtept apart behold battaile wold meddle becauſe hee beene ſo well receiued feaſted citie towne hee well perceiued aſſaults realme perſia howe admirall coozen barnard whereof ſuch ioy hee wept gladneſſe thanked god good fortune ſent ſaid ah good lord thou oughteſt greatly prayſed thou neuer fayleſt time néede ſerue thée nowe may well ſay thy gracious ayd yet ſhall ſee wife child thus huon ſaide himſelfe beholding battailes fighting chap cxxiii ¶ city colander taken admirall perſia hadde wonne battaile great ioy made vnto huon hee knowne admirall perſia cozen barnard admirall perſia ſawe perceiued towne yſſued marched foorth battailes ſet vpon enemy great ſlaughter made part laſt citie worſt chriſtian men greater number paynim sarazins yſſued wherefore conſtrained graunt victorie enemy paynim retired fled towards citie admirall barnard company chaced ſlew pity ſée finally admirall oppreſſed ſo ſore hee entred citie barnard companie ſlew beat sarazins great maruaile ſee bloud ranne ſtréets admirall ſaw hee victorie hée commaunded ceaſe ſlaying ſuch would beleeue lorde god liues ſhould bee ſaued good ſo ſuch would bee chriſtened ſhould bee ſlaine incontinent none ſpared done many receiued chriſtendome many woulde receiue ſlaine thus citie taken huon entred citie admiral men came pallaice whereas hee ſawe admirall baron barnard coozen huon ſtill mall vppon necke came hall put helmet ſaluted admirall admirall lord ſaw huon great ioy tongue tell oh right déere vertuous knight quoth admirall comming doth ſo reioyce cannot tell whether dreame much bound vnto god hee hath giuen grace ſaue perill admirall embraced huon may well know barnard coozen great ioy ſo admirall ſayd vnto huon sir pray ſhew mee aduentures haue ſince departed v huon ſhewed yée haue heard héere eſcaped admirall vnderſtood huon neuer ſo amazed abaſhed liues hée ſo eſcaped handes diuell ſayd hée much bound vnto god glad right ioyfull comming huon eſpecially barnard captaine citie newly receiued chriſtendome came vnto huon ſayd sir require deſire admirall bée good lord maiſter promiſed faithfully abide heere towne good true seruant keeping firmely chriſtian faith haue newly receiued huon ſaw captaine receiued houſe firſt comming citie went vnto admirall ſaid sir require chap cxxv ¶ anſwere admirall perſia medium made vnto souldans meſſenger report made vnto maiſter admirall well heard vnderſtood souldans meſſenger beganne ſmile ſaid tell thy maiſter ſet nothing thou maiſt haue thou flyeſt away thus alone without company turne thy ſhéeld againſt mée elſe ſhall ſlay thée flying souldan well heard huon hee hadde great maruaile greatly feared hée knew well whome receiued ſo great loſſe damage whome many kinges admiral béene ſlaine thought himſelfe hée returned hee ſhould bee ſlaine wherefore tooke courage himſelfe ſeeing huon alone aſwell alſo hee thought ſhould long ſuccoured ſome men followed therefore like hardy knight turned horſe head towards huon fiercely ranne one another gaue great ſtroakes béene vnto souldan ſmall profite hee béene reſcued men come huon ſlaine thether came fortie knightes sarazins ranne huon ſore diſmayed abaſhed ſawe himſelfe ſo incloſed enemy howbeit hee might haue ſaued himſelfe well ynough liſted haue fledde away feare ioy abbot couent lord ʋergier ſhewed whole diſcourſe diſcomfiture booty deuided amongeſt wonne men warre departed except thowſand men whome abbot retayned ſauegard towne cluny made many ſkirmiſhes emperours menne diſcomfiture newes thereof preſently brought citie mayence emperour tirrey right ſorrowfull death nephew ſiſters ſonne reaſon ſorrow great diſpleaſure hee thrée dayes would come foorth chamber fourth day ſent lord councell made complaint occaſion duke huon bourdeaux loſt foure nephew baſtard ſonne ſaid ought greatly gréeued cannot bée reuenged huon thinke hee ſhall neuer returne againe ſéeing ſo take vengeance ſhall take vppon wife eſcleremond vppon thrée hundred priſoners brought burdeaux ſame lord made fourmed mee ſemblance ſhall neuer haue ioy heart eate drinke vntill haue ſeene eſcleremond burnt fire thrée hundred priſoners hanged ſtrangled wil knowe ſpeaketh firſt contrarie ſhall hate euer lord well heard emperour make promiſe none ſo hardy durſt ſpeake one woord emperour commaunded haſt great plentie thornes caried citie vnto little mountaine beſide reared vp certaine gallowes hange thereon thrée hundred priſoners done hee commaunded tenne load thornes caried burne noble ladie eſcleremond ſhe ſent priſon foure hangman priſoners brought citie bée beaten way noble ladie ſaw ſhee dealt withall ſhee pitiouſly complained good huſband huon daughter clariet ſaide ah right ſwéet lord huſband huon time ſhall bee departure v two ſhee called vppon lord ieſus chriſt praying grace pity bring ſoule paradice thus cry complayning noble ladie ledde towne lady burgeſſes maiden citie ranne windowes dores beheld dolourous pitifull companie leading towardes death ſayd high ah right noble ladie become great beautie woont bee viſage pale diſcoloured woont ſo faire nowe ſo loathed diſfigured become faire haires nowe bee ſo blacke rugged great pouertie haue endured ala noble ladie great pitie compaſſion haue ſée eſtate could amend thus ladie led towne ſhe bemoned ſawe three hundred gentleman alſo led forth emperour tirrey lord road deſire ſee noble ladie burnt priſoners hanged hee made haſt becauſe ſorrow hee death nephewe men newly ſlaine meanes abbot cluny yſſued citie mayence duke hildebert néere kinſman emperours comming citie ſame time ladie ledde foorth hée ſawe rudely dealt ladie ſawe knew well faire ladie eſcleremond hee ſawe point water eye ſayd vnto ledde sir go faſt vntill haue ſpoken emperour gladly noble ladie eſcleremond well heard vnderſtood duke ſhee ſome little hope ſhee turned eye towards ſayd ah right noble prince haue pittie compaſſion mee haue done nothinge whereby ſhould deſerue die duke well vnderſtood ſuch pitie could ſpeake word heart ſo full ſorrowe road faſt might méet emperour paſſed thrée hundred priſoners great pity compaſſion ſo came vnto emperour wéeping ſaid ah right noble emperour require honour paſſion lord ieſus chriſt haue pitie compaſſion dolourous companie likely die day remember nowe holy time lent wherefore require reſpite liues vntill paſt eaſter sir humbly require ſeruice mine haue done vnto graunt requeſt reward reaſonable iuſt great wronge doe reuenge anger vppon noble ladie haue chaced countrey landes signiories hold handes take reuenewes profit thereof▪ bee ſufficed doubt lord ieſus chriſt ſore diſpleaſed emperour well heard duke cozen hee ſtoode ſtill ſpake haſtely ſayd faire coozen haue well heard therefore anſweare briefe wordes men bee mine empire prieſtes frier preach vnto whole yeare deſiring reſpite lady death would doe nothing therefore ſpeake matter beard hangeth vnder chinne ſince cannot haue huon huſband ſhall neuer eat drinke vntill haue ſéene burnt perſons hanged remember death nephewes deare sonne haue béen ſlaine huon member bodie trembleth ſorrow diſpleaſure good duke hildebert vnderſtood emperour hee great ſorrowe heart departed without word ſpeaking without leaue taking returned thence hee became full yre diſpleaſure emperour tirrey cryed hye voyce ſayde howe would ſhortly diſpatch matter ſée ye lady burnt ledde hill whereas fire readie ladie perceiued place whereas ſhee ſhould die ſhee caſt great crie made pitifull complaint lord ieſus chriſt ſayd ah right ſweet lord ieſus chriſt thou knoweſt loue thée chriſtened beléeue thy lawes wherein liue die ſée well dayes ſhort thou knoweſt well cauſe wherein haue deſerued death therefore require thee humbly haue pitie compaſſion soule thou wilt vouchſafe kéepe preſerue huſband huon daughter clariet thus yee haue heard noble ducheſſe eſcleremond made complaint handes bound kneeling vppon knées ſtake abiding houre death nowe let v leaue ſpeake noble ladie vntill haue occaſion returne againe ſpeake noble king oberon companie chap cxxxiii ¶how king oberon ſent twoo knight lady fayrie diuers knighte • ſame making great ioye king oberon ſitting 〈…〉 throne garniſhed bordered fine gould precious ſtones hee ſat hee fell great ſtudie therewith droppes water fell eye began wéepe complaine ſo ſore though ſhould haue drowned droppes water theſe quéenes lady damſels ſawe make ſuch ſorrow great maruell gloriand good knighte frayrie mallabron right priuie welbeloued king oberon ſaw kinge make ſuch ſorrow ſore diſmayed abaſhed sir gloriand ſaide sir man liuinge world hath diſpleaſed done thing againſt gloriand quoth kinge diſpleaſure haue faire ladie eſcleremond wife vnto duke huon bourdeaux verie good fréend ſhe led citie mayence brought vnto great fire wherein emperour tirrey burne three hundred poore priſoners bee hanged may ayd ſuccour right ſorrie thereof loue huon paſſed sea way returning homeward hee hath ſuch aduentures humane bodie could ſuffer beare paine trauailes hee hath endured maruailous aduentures hee hath borne hath ſo many battailes great maruaile woonderfull heare rehearſed whereas hee thought haue reſt haue found wife faire ladie eſcleremond aliue ſhall burnt except ſhee bee ſhortly aided ſuccoured ſure hee die ſorrowe griefe hee haue heart gloriand mallabron well hearde vnderſtood kinge oberon kneeled downe king ſayde sir wee deſire ſuccour noble ladie loue good huſband deare fréend huon gloriand quoth noble kinge oberon doe well content haſtely goe deliuer good ladie priſoners ſay behalfe emperour tirrey hee ſo hardy doe ill ladie companie ſay commaund reſpite liues vntill holy feaſt eaſter paſſed ladie priſoners cauſe returned againe citie mayence ladie ſet chamber libertie pleaſure let bathed waſhed newe arrayed lette haue foure noble lady ſe • ue accompanie ſhe haue meat drinke good plentifull though ſhe owne proper daughter like wiſe lette priſoners ſerued ſay commaund hée doth thus vntill time eaſter paſſed ſhew bee ſo hardy breake treſpaſſe againſt commaundement gloriand mallabron tooke leaue kinge wiſhed themſelues place whereas ladie priſoners lady vppon knee fire ſore wéeping complayning abiding houre death beene néere vnto ſhe béen ſhortly ſuccoured haue bound ſtake gloriand mallabron came braying ayre like thunder ſéen perſon alonely ladie come ſawe fire kindling tooke tenne villaines would haue caſt ladie fire tooke caſt ten flaming fire whereas ſhortly burnt beſide diuers burnt whereof ſuch ſo great feare none durſt abide two knight came ladie loozed ſayd madame good comfort wée two knight ſent hether king oberon ſuccour bring perill danger sir quoth ladie firſt time noble king oberon hath ſuccoured v mee huſband god grace rewarde madame quoth gloriand bee merrie make ioy good huſband huon come ſide sea whome ſhall ſée within ſhort time good ladie well vnderſtood gloriand ſhee ſuch ioy great ſpace ſhe could ſpeake word ſhee ſo rauiſhed laſt ſhe ſaid sir ought greatly loue bringing ſuch tidings ſayde vnto madame reſt héere ſeaſon vntill wee haue deliuered priſoners whome ſée yonder leading toward death ſhortly ſhall returne againe vnto therewith departed ladie left vpon knées holding vp handes vnto heauen deuoutly rendring thankes lord ieſus chriſt ſuccor aide ſent gloriand mallabron came gallowes vnloozed thrée hundred priſoners ſ • ew diuers ſent thether doe execution whereof preſent great maruaile woonder thereat ſaw company ſlaine could ſée thought thouſand knight reaſon great brute noyſe two knight fayrie made whereof ſuch feare fled away ranne emperour ſore diſmayed abaſhed aduenture alſo ſhewed vnto ladie reſcued could tell ſayd heard great brute noyſe alſo emperour ſaw people came running towards flying gallowes ſhewed ſéen heard wherof emperour lordes great feare ſore abaſhed ah sir quoth duke auſtrich hadde beene better haue beleeued duke hildebert coozen knowe ſurely haue greatly diſpleaſed lord ieſus chriſt ſince would doe ſuch cruell iuſtice holy time lent thus theſe two knight fayrie hadde reſcued good ladie priſoners tooke ladie brought vnto emperour ſhewed themſelues openly preſence emperour priſoners emperour ſaw twoo knightes armed vppon horſebacke hee ſet little ſaid ſo bolde ſo hardy deliuer take men handes thoſe condemned die iuſtice beſides haue ſlaine many men nowe bringe preſence haue condemned die wherefore well know eat drinke ſhalbe hanged ladie eſcleremond burned ſhall depart hence vntill haue ſeen dye death gloriand mallabron lifted vp viſors ſhewed face ſéemed vnto ſawe neuer ſawe two ſo faire knightes liues gloriand ſayde vnto emperour sir threatninges wee make thereof little account sir knowe troth noble king oberon commandeth v much feare life bee ſo hardy doe ill iniurie commaund bee done vnto noble ladie heere preſent theſe priſoners vntill eaſter day bee paſt alſo kinge oberon commaundeth doe keepe ladie houſe cloathed apparelled well gouerned bee accompanied lady damſels ſerue honourably well ſhe owne proper daughter like wiſe theſe priſoners newly arrayed ordered aſwell knight houſe sir warne charge wee haue ſayd contrarie thing may fall otherwiſe mortall man ſhall ſaue life thus right noble kinge oberon commaundeth doe soueraigne lord gouernor realme fayrie emperour tirrey well heard theſe knightes fayrie thus ſpeake vnto ſawe howe armed swordes handes taynted bloud almaynes hee great feare beheld baron ſayde sir pray giue ſome good counſaile ſerious buſineſſe wee haue well heard much ſpeaking king oberon great act déeds wherefore feare much yée may wel ſée two knight haue done haue reſcued haue condemned die ſlaine diuers men alſo heare word ſendeth two knight ſhould keepe ladie priſoners honourably ſhould ſo hardy put danger vntill eaſter paſſed ancient knight ſayd sir know troth king oberon puiſſant wiſe nothing world knoweth alſo often hée liſt hee bee whereas wiſh himſelfe great number people hee liſt therefore sir beléeue ſurely doe otherwiſe hath commaunded doe theſe twoo knightes héere preſent haue puiſſance ſufficient deſtroy kinge oberon ſit ſtill home therefore sir mine aduiſe anſweare theſe two knight kinge oberon hath commaunded doe doe ſurely lordes gaue emperour ſame counſaile emperour well heard vnderſtood lordes baron turned vnto two knightes fayrie ſaid sir yée ſhall ſalute king oberon ſay ſhall doe euerie thing hee hath commaunded doe beſt power sir emperour quoth gloriand doe ſay king take fréend therevppon commend god thus two knight departed ſo emperour none perſon knew become whereof euerie man great maruaile ſore abaſhed thus gloriand mallabron within came city momur whereas found king oberon whome ſhewed done well quoth king oberon lady eſcleremond priſoners eaſe well ſerued moneth paſſed ſhall dearely ab • eaſe bee nowe emperour hateth ſo ſore becauſe malice beareth vnto huon bourdeaux ſet againe priſon great pouertie miſerie eaſter paſſed hee burne ladie eſcleremond hange vp priſoners except bee reſcued againe sir quoth gloriand cannot beléeue emperour dare doe thinke ſo doe gloriand quoth noble kinge oberon know ſurely great hate rooted heart emperour ſhall conſtraine vrge thus • e nowe let v leaue ſpeaking noble king oberon ſpeake emperour tirrey chap cxxxiiii ¶how emperour tirrey made noble ladie eſcleremond well ſerued apparelled priſoners three weekes hee made noble ladie ſayd priſoners put againe priſon whereas great miſerie nowe ſheweth hiſtorie two knightes fayrie departed vaniſhed away preſence emperour emperor returned citie mayence ladie eſcleremond priſoners whereof burgeſſes lady damſels citie great ioy good aduenture emperour pallaice deliuered vnto chamber well dreſt hanged appertained thereunto noble ducheſſe eſcleremond hadde foure lady ſerue ſhe bathed waſhed new apparelled well richly though ſhee beene emperours owne proper daughter ſo within ſhort ſpace ſhe came againe beautie faire well fauoured euer ſhe like wiſe ſo priſoners kept alſo faire rich chamber new apparelled eaſe pleaſures knight emperor court aſſoone thrée weekes paſſed great hate emperour vnto noble ladie priſoners conſtrained take ioy eaſe turned ſame pitifull weepinges great lamentation emperour tirrey ſware kinge oberon thinge could doe would neuer peace heart vntill ſet companie againe intd priſon beſides ſware eaſter ſhould bee ſooner paſt ladie eſcleremond ſhould bee burnt priſoners hanged vppon take vengeance deſpite huon bourdeaux done ſo much trouble hee could forget hee commaunded take againe ducheſſe eſcleremond put priſoners priſon againe done according commandement ducheſſe eſcleremond priſoners right ſorrowfull great feare ſaide ala deathes approach ladie ſawe ſhe ſet againe priſon ſhe began ſore weepe complaine duke huon huſband longe quoth ſhee tarie ſée none way death approacheth ſhall come time well may curſe houre euer borne life haue ſorrowe heauineſſe dolour ſupportable better mee haue béen dead ſpend life darke priſon right deuoutly ſhee called vppon lorde ieſus chriſt haue pittie compaſſion thus noble ducheſſe ſet againe priſon alſo thrée hundred priſoners whereas ſuffered great famine pouertie thing liue barley bread cleare water leaue ſpeake ſpeake duke huon arriued marſellis chap cxxxv ¶ huon departed marſellis came ʋncle good abbot cluny habite diſguiſed vnto diſcouered himſelfe whereof abbot great ioy ſo clariet daughter yee haue heard heere howe huon marſellis hee iourned foure dayes hee made readie depart bought mule horſes himſelfe barnard companie hee charged somers vppon one hee truſſed griffens foote great horrible couered becauſe euerie man ſhoulde ſée hee readie euerie thing truſſed hee departed marſellis roade ſo iourneys hee paſſed prouence came vnto maſconoys vppon thurſday night arriued towne tournous ſupped hée called barnard coozen ſayd coozen pray ſtay héere wil goe ſée mine vncle good abbot cluny clariet daughter whome ſore deſire ſée ſhortly ſhall returne againe vnto goe priuily diſguiſed entent bee knowne sir quoth barnard ſéeing pleaſure muſt content went bed morning huon aroſe vp apparelled himſelfe like pilgrim ſtaffe hand bag necke great boot vppon legges hee hadde great beard long haire wherefore hee ſéemed well pilgrime came farre countrey ſo done indéede barnard company ſawe ſo apparelled laughed ſaide sir appeareth well manner eſcaped ſome good place ſéemeth v ſhake ſtaffe make money auoyd men purſes ſo bold beggar huon heard hee laughed tooke leaue departed alone bagge necke ſo afoote hée went vntill came vnto cluny came vnto abbey gate called porter vnto ſayd fréend pray let mée enter hée opened wicket beheld huon ſéemed tal goodly man ſayd pilgrime enter pleaſe huon entred wicket ſayde vnto porter fréende come ſtraight beyond great sea haue kiſſed holy sepulchre haue ſuffered much paine pouertie becauſe time haue béene héere abbot place therefore thought would paſſe without ſpeaking pray ſhewe mee courteſie may ſpeake hée ſoone know mée sir quoth porter ſéemeth vnto mee manner ſéeme man good place therefore giue leaue goe houſe pleaſure ſhall finde good abbot hall whereas hee communing brother certainly knowe well ſhall bee welcome vnto hee haue knowledge noble man courteous liberall ſhall find vpon ſide sea fréend quoth huon courteſie may auaile huon went hall whereas hee found abbot brother hee ſaluted abbot couent fréend quoth abbot welcome pray ſhewe mée whence come sir quoth huon ſhall ſhew troth come beyond sea holy city ieruſalem whereas haue kiſſed holy sepulchre lord ieſus chriſt quicke dead haue béen thoſe part seauen yéeres cauſe come hether ſée found young knight mine age named huon bourdeaux ſayd nephew ſaw would depart thence come countrey humbly prayed mée recommend vnto therefore come vnto doe meſſuage hath together diuers battailes great amitie haue béen betweene v good abbot well heard vnderſtood pilgrim many teares fell eye trickled downe chéekes heard nephew huon named ſaide fréende pray bee true ſay ſhew mée troth haue ſéen nephew huon loue beſt world deſire moſt ſée pray ſhewe vnto mée minde either returne hether elſe abide ſtill would god debt pay thouſand markes gould ſo hee héere hall sir quoth huon nephew whome deſire ſo much ſée moneth paſt grace god bee héere sir hee ſhewed mée departing hath daughter haue nouriſhed brought vp charged greatly ſhould deſire ſée departed knoweth whether ſhe bee aliue dead woulde gladly ſée pleaſure fréend quoth abbot right gladly ſhall ſée ſhall cauſe come hether may ſée eaſe dare well ſay vnto world ſhall find fairer ſweeter creature wiſer age better learned yet ſhe ten yeares age huon vnderſtood abbot may well know hee hadde great ioy heart priuily thanked lord ieſus chriſt abbot called vnto right notable knight named sir emerie commaunded goe fetch thether néece clariet knight went chamber whereas faire ladie foure noble lady brought vp sir emerie ſaluted ladie young ladie perceiued sir emerie ſhe aroſe vp rendred ſalutation right humbly ſaying sir knight ioyfull commig pray ſhewe mee newes tidinges certainly faire ladie quoth knight hether come pilgrim come beyond sea hee hath ſhewed vnto abbot vncle tidinges father duke huon therefore vncle deſireth come ſpeake ladie heard ſpeaking father heart ſhe deſired knowe ſome certaine tidinges ſhee damſels departed chamber came hall abbot vncle accompanied twoo notable knightes ſhee entred hall richly apparelled man could deſcribe beautie ſhee ſo well fourmed nature ſelfe could amend ſkinne white flower meadowe coloured like red roſe haunch lowe pappes ſomewhat ryſing throat ſmooth cleare chinne vaunted mouth vermeill roſe téeth ſmall well ranged white face white well coloured mingled white red eye ſmiling chéere amourous behoulde noſe ſtraight forehead white haire yellowe eares gentle cloſe cannot deuiſe tenth part excellent beautie none could regard looke vppon praiſed loued beautie ſweete demeanour great humilitie ſhoulde héere deſcribe would bee ouerlong rehearſe huon well ſéene daughter clariet ſo faire hee gladly behelde without making knowledge abbot tooke néece hand ledde vnto huon ſaid pilgrim ſay ſhee hath beene ſore trauailed much come sunne haue kept long time ſhe garniſhed beauty like wiſe ſo ſhe witte bountie ſhee daughter vnto duke huon bourdeaux man moſt loue world woulde god ſée doe nowe god ſend mee life health ladie ſhall bee richly maried giue good ſhe ſhalbe rich puiſſant sir quoth huon pray lord ieſus chriſt giue good fortune ſhee may bee ſo maried bloud thereby may lifted vp exalted faire ladie clariet ſayd vnto huon sir pilgrim pray ſhewe know tidings father duke huon bourdeaux faire ladie quoth huon hee together haue beene long time beyond sea companion together ſought souldan babilon nowe hee ſet huon ſlaine great admirall gaudiſe another ſince time conquered citie countrey egipt many aduentures huon haue ſuffered end wee diſcomfited souldan men ſlaine deſtroyed pilgrim quoth faire ladie clariet require ſhew know whether deare father returne hether thing world moſt deſire faire ladie quoth anſweare twoo moneths bee paſſed ſhall ſée héere good health pray vnto lord god quoth ladie may ſo may deliuer mother priſon whereas ſhee great pouertie miſerie huon well heard vnderſtood daughter would longer hide himſelfe ſayd right deare daughter auguſt paſſed ſhall deliuer die paine ſhall make ſuch warre againſt emperour tirrey yet die ſhall ſtrike head bodie whatſoeuer fall thereof ladie heard huon ſayd hee father ſhee changed colour bluſhed ruddie roſe thought ſelfe word ſpake hee father whereof ſhe right ioyfull ſaid ah sir pray bee duke huon bourdeaux father ſhew right deare daughter beléeue ſurely longer hide ladie heard father ſhe clipped twentie time kiſſed abbot came embraced ſayd right deare nephewe ioy heart hath comming mee ſo acceptable cannot tell whether dreame ſée heere againe hee embraced making greateſt ioy world alſo clariet daughter embraced kiſſed houſe came thether make great chéere feaſting faire nephewe quoth abbot ſore abaſhed mounted vpon horſes ducheſſe rich littour ſo departed citie mayence ceaſed till came within twoo league abbey cluny good abbot knew nothing agréement made betwéene emperour huon gathered together men warre twentie thouſand lodged towne cluny abbot aduertiſed emperours comming thoſe part heard newes huon whereof right ſorrowfull ſore diſpleaſed thought emperour hadde taken huon priſoner hee yſſued towne ranged men good order battaile without towne faireplaine abiding emperour whome ſaw comming chap cxl ¶ emperour arriued cluny abbot ſet vpon peace made emperour conueyed huon bourdeaux rendred alſo muſt néedes ſpeake goe bourdeaux ſame time abbot mounted puiſſant ſtrong courſer well armed point ſawe emperour comming towards cluny ſaid men sir thinke day doe well valiantly yonder v may ſée emperour enemie comming wherefore wée cannot eſcape battaile ſure hath taken huon nephew faith owe lord saint bennet patron taking ſhalbe déerely bought couched ſpeares ſpurred horſes came running towards emperour emperour ſaw hee called huon ſaid sir yonder yée may ſée men warre armed come running againſt v wot meane doe ſéeme enemy far perceiue great number therfore doubted feared sir quoth huon mine vncle abbot cluny hath rayſed vp men ſuccour aduertiſed peace made betwéen mée ſurely thinketh haue taken priſoner therewith abbot daſhed amongeſt emperours companie firſt met ran cleane ſpeare ſo ſerued ſecond third fourth ſpeare broken hee drew ſwoord wherewith beat downe almaines maruaile behould came men ſuch deed armes perforce almaines faine retire backe many ſlaine deſtroyed caſt downe earth emperour ſaw hee great rage ſayd vnto huon sir greatly blame ſuffer vncles men ſlay mine sir quoth huon right ſorrie haue done readie make amendes whatſoeuer ſhall pleaſe therewith duke huon road vnto good abbot vncle great diſpleaſure ſayd vncle haue done great euill abbot ſaw perceiued huon right ioyfull hee embraced ſaid faire nephew thought emperour taken priſoner would haue put death knew peace made men retire backe almaines hee huon together came vnto emperour abbot ſaluted ſaid sir pray pardon haue thus come againſt certainly thought would haue hanged ſlaine nephew duke huon bourdeaux knew peace betwéene therefore sir require pardon mée offer ſelfe make amends aduice counſaile sir quoth emperour pardon loue beare vnto duke huon bourdeaux whome take faithfull ſpeciall fréend thus yée haue heard peace made betwéene emperour abbot cluny road together vntill came vnto cluny emperour receiued great ioy good abbot hadde receiued emperour lodged abbey came vnto ducheſſe eſcleremond embraced kiſſed ſayde right déere néece comming vnto mee hether greatly acceptable well pleaſed ſée whole good health ſore diſpleaſed great euils pouerties haue endured might abbot ſuch puniſhment neuer ſo ill aduenture fell vnto mée therefore sir haue ſhewed vnto euerie thing ſuffer mee depart vnto companie monke quoth huon let thée go vntill thou haſt ſhewed vnto manner way may goe vntill haue found kinge oberon thus huon monke talked together vntill faire day light huon looked round ſaw neither caſtle church rocke riuer hee ſawe faire meadowe whereof huon eſcleremond ſore abaſhed bleſſed hauing great maruaile ſéen monke deſired huon let go monke quoth huon drawe ſtruggle cannot auaile thee thou ſhalt eſcape handes vntill thou haſt ſhewed citie momur whereas king oberon huon quoth monke content doe firſt pray thée take necke ſtole monke quoth huon thy reaſoning cannot auaile thée thou ſhalt eſcape vntill thou haſt ſet wife néere vnto citie momur thou ſhalt goe v foote foote well quoth monke ſince thus content fulfill pleaſure one thinge ſay vnto neuer wiſer deed would let goe away ſtole wherewith doe hold precious ſtones haue ſhold neuer haue departed hence thought haue beguiled ſo might haue let mée gone wayes whether would goe monke quoth huon ſhall depart vntill haue ſet mee wife within citie momur sir quoth monke doe cannot doe though would ſhall ſette vppon mount hircama thence may well ſée vnto citie momur countrey fayrie returne vnto companie time paſſed great sea • rta • monke quoth huon content ſo thou wilt ſette v place ſaw neither towne caſtle wherof ſore abaſhed recommended themſelues vnto lord god went foorth meadow could ſee neither towne caſtle houſe village man demaund way went ſo long came foote mountaine polliſhed ſhine ſo bright againſt sunne though chriſtall huon ſaid vnto wife madame yonder v may ſée noble citie momur whereas king oberon sir quoth eſcleremond lord god hath done vnto v great grace hee hath brought v hether ſauegard perſons went foorth vntill came néere vnto citie momur citie ſawe maruailous great riuer verie déepe two bowe ſhoots largeneſſe maruailous pleaſant behould came riuerſide founde man little veſſel awaiting vppon woulde come vnto citie paſſe ouer huon eſcleremond wife entred little shippe ſaluted guider thereof hee woulde giue none aunſweare maruailouſly behelde ouer marriner named clarimodes sonne damſell fayrie demaunded huon wife ſayd mée thinkes none fayrie wherefore content haue paſſed ouer huon gaue none aunſweare went foorth entred citie paſſed greatly regarded within citie ſayd one another great maruaile ſée theſe two perſons enter citie king oberon lyeth ſicke bedde gaue great charge vnto clarimodes ſtraunger ſhould paſſe riuer enter citie way betwéene hoaſt towne valiant knight sir peter aragon florence eſpyed ſo made haſt afore hee ſawe time ſet vppon enemy florence ſore deſirous fulfill promiſe king father tooke speare encountred knight ſuch vertue ranne cleane drawing speare nauarnes fel downe dead florence ſayd god hath giuen mee good beginning hee drewe ſword ſtrake another vppon helmet ſuch ſort claue head teeth third fourth hee made dolorouſly die hee neuer ceaſed vntill ſlaine tenne enemy thus vnder meadowes courtoys horrible battaile betwéen nauarnes aragon vpon partes ſuch ſlaughter great maruaile behold anon florence ſword well knowne force armes brake great preaſſes vppon ſoeuer ſtroke lighted hee either ſlaine caſt earth euerie man feared ſo much none durſt abide approach néere vnto ſame time florence battaile dooing maruailes faire damſell clariet vppon wals citie lady damſels regarding hye proweſſe florence field ioy ſhe thereof ſoone turned ſorrow wéepings king garyn could forget mortall hate liueth hee ſhall neuer ſee whatſoeuer fall thereof therefore goe way take caſt sea amonge greateſt waues finde theſe knightes vnderſtood king commaunded doe murder right ſorrowfull heartes durſt ſay nay doe againſt knewe well ſhould die knew neither mercie pitie therefore durſt make ſemblance contrarie feared ſo much diſpleaſe went tooke damſell whereas ſhee sir quoth ſhee doe mee wherefore doe take mée let mee goe haue thing mee ſhew mée ſayd damſell ſpeake end come ſhall neuer ſee faire day ſhe ſaw ſhe ſo taken tenne men went threatning ſlay ſhee caſt great crie deſired god ayd ſuccour bound damſels handes cord ſuch manner white tender ſkinne burſt bound ſo ſore bloud dropped nayles sir quoth ſhe crie mercie little ſhall winne ſlay mee ſhall doe great ſin ſeeing haue deſerued madame quoth wordes cannot auaile kinge ſhall make auaunt haue sonne mariage ſhalbe drowned sea whether wéeping ſhall ayd foure ribaulds tooke bound drew haire head led toward seaſide haue drowned often time ſayd god haue ſaued cannot periſhed ſame ſeaſon florence battaile whereas hee fought enemy sir peter aragon taken many priſoners hee came vnto florence ſayd ah sir require let v returne citie bee content haue done day yonder may ſée comming al whole hoaſt nauarnes againſt poſſible v endure thréeſcore thouſand men hate v death haue done ynough ought content take none ſaue life coozen quoth florence pray depart let mee iuſt mine vncle kinge nauarre whome haue promiſed yéeld priſoner vnto king father thereby ſhall haue mariage faire damſell loue loue faire damſell ſhal make many nauernoys looſe liues sir quoth peter ſince deſire owne death right ſorrie thereof longer tarie héere poſſible v tarie héere without bee ſlaine wilfully haue héere many priſoners go lead citie ſhall returne vnto entent either taken priſoner wee may bee redéemed againe peter went citie priſoners come citie hee heard great noiſe market place whereof hee great maruaile went thether hee ſawe foure foule villaines drawing faire damſell clariet towardes seaſide drowne ſaw hee neuer ſo ſorrowfull life incontinent let goe priſoners drew ſword cryed vnto led damſell ah yée falſe théeues let damſell go brought beyond sea yée neuer ſuch folly liues therewith hée ſtrake firſt sword ſuch ſort head ſlewe bodie ſecond hee claue téeth third fourth hee ſlewe faire ladie ſaw earle peter right pitifully ſhe outrage worthy beare crown sonne florence ought haue traytour ought hould realme full déerely ſhall abuy ill damſell make abaſhed hee made ſemblance runne vppon king ſword feare ran chamber ſhut faſt sompterhorſe come battaile skirmiſh maiſter thinke hee ſhall haue worſe company almaine hearing ſo ſpeake ſayd faire sonne thou ſayſt procéedeth good courage therefore good muſt come thée yet pray thée ſhew mee thy name sir quoth ſhee called ide brother quoth almaine entertain thée ſeruice take héed horſe sir quoth ſhe ready doe beſt ſeruice ſo almaine lodging thus ſhe ſerued woont ſerued ſhee feared ſhould perceiued ſhe woman wold trouble therefore ſhe kept ſelfe cloſe ſecret ſhe continued thrée dayes maiſter company gone towardes roome maſter might depart ſo ſoone buſineſſe readie thrée dayes departed go roome ſhee armed cuſtome countrey ſhe ſerued maiſter ſo well hee prayſed long road came approached neere countrey rome ſo day entred great darke forreſt wherein lay ambuſhment seauenſcore spaniard lying abide aduenture lay darke valley ſaw almaines diſpiſed death ranne vppon ide road maſter couched speare ſtrake spaniard therewith cleane bodie drawing speare spaniard fell downe dead courſe maiſter praiſed spaniard ran among almaines right valiantly defended themſelues defence could auaile end ſlaine ſo none eſcaped aliue alonely ide beare ſelfe ſo valiantly ſhee ſlewe foure spaniard ſhe ſaw maiſter companie wer ſlain ſword hand bloudie ſhe fled away road way tooke little path brought rocke ſhe alighted taried wood night vntill next morning ſhe ſo great hunger thirſt ſhe néere hand famiſhed ſhe ridden day without meat drinke morning ſhe looked al ſawe arbour thirtie théeues ſitting table eating drinking pleaſure damſell ſaw great rage hunger ſhe ſuffered conſtrained ſuch wiſe ſhe forgat feare went vnto théeues ſaw one ſayd fellowes ſee yonder comming squier mounted vpon good horſe ſhalbe ide approached ſhee humbly ſaluted companie ſayd sir may pleaſe let eate drinke pay ſhotte fréende quoth one man hath beene guide forreſt sir quoth ide god hath beene conduct none one theeues ſtept forth tooke horſe bridle ſaid companie sir lay ſtrike downe ſhall neuer eate drinke horſe ſhall eſcape damſell ſaw ſhe taken ſhe great feare ſhee durſt make countenance defend ſelfe ſo many theeues vpon ſhe thought humble ſelfe ſhould bee profit ſayd sir make haſt ſlay mee little ſhall yee winne thereby looze hold heere ſword yeild ſelfe handes pray honour ieſus chriſt giue ſome meat drinke ſo hungrie almoſt famiſhed maſter theefe ſayd squier haue feare ſtriken thou ſhalt haue hurt ſelfe thou ſhalt haue thou lackeſt goe thy way ſit downe eat drinke thy pleaſure sir quoth ide thanke damſell ſate downe eat drinke pleaſure eaten riſen vp théeues beganne ſtriue among themſelues ſaying chiefe maiſter howe hee done ill would ſuffer ſlay squier another anſweared ſaid ſhould hurt done vnto becauſe hee ſo faire young man ſo courteous ſayde ſhould great dammage ſlay better kéepe ſtill learne ſteale murder men ſo doe good reaſon ſlay ide vnderſtood théeues ſhe great feare called vpon lord god praying humbly great néede ayd ſuccour chiefe maiſter demaunded spaniard ambuſhment lying valley ſo ſet vppon v ſlewe company none eſcaped ſelfe therefore sir pray let mee haue againe horſe ſword ſhew mee way rome would great almes deede ſhew courteſie nay quoth maiſter théefe doe thou ſhalt tarrie v learne thiefe murderer thou wilt thus doe sword ſhall ſtrike thy head sir quoth ide would haue thing neuer accuſtomed doe none lineage haue intention doe ſuch workes therefore pray lette haue horſe ſword doe great courteſie mounted vpon horſe one defie defend ſelfe ſtrike head haue bought meate drinke verie déere ſhould looze horſe maiſter théefe ſayd becauſe ſée thou art ſo hardy wraſtle thee vpon couenant thou caſt thou ſhalt one companie thou caſt earth haue thy horſe thy sword ſpoyle thee thy cloathes ide ſayd content thus ſo withdraw men ſet horſe ſword tyed ſaddle bowe common prouerbe man taken foole putteth truſt theefe theues heard could forbare laughing great deſire ſee wraſtling betwixt withdrew backe ſet horſe noble damſell ide quickly tooke théefe thought haue borne earth ſhee drew ſo ſore could ſcarce haue breath therewith ſhee caſt ſo rudely earth againſt ſtone therewith ſwound fall teeth burſt mouth ide ſaw théefe danger ſhe went quickely horſe mounted vp ſhe drew ſword▪ ſayd ah ye vilde théeues treaſon ſhall auaile ye haue thought violence treaſon againſt mee goe helpe maiſter lyeth yonder thinke ſhall euer remember wraſt • ing v haue doubt though hundred ſhall make bee hanged ſtrangled quickeſt lighteſt théefe amonge ſtept foorth tooke bridle horſe ſhee ſawe ſhee lifted vp sword ſtrake théefe vpon hand ſo hand flew bodie hanged ſtill vppon bridle hee ranne away thinking die paine hande ſhe daſht among théeues weapon defend themſelues withall folly feare fell beléeued ſuch young squier ſhould haue hadde ſuch hardnes force ſhee fought fiercely among cut armes ſhoulders claue ſome braines ſhe ſo much ſhe ſlew fiue théeues ſhe dep • rted ſhe ſaw time depart ſhe ſpurred horſe time reſidue théeues gotten weapon followed haue ſlaine horſe ſhée departed ſpurres horſe good therefore anon ſhe farre théeues ſawe loſt labour follow therefore let goe ide ſaw ſhe eſcaped handes ſhe humbly thanked lord god deſiring ayd conduct ſome ſauegard ſhe road ſo long ſhe yſſued great forreſt iourneys lodging make mention ſhe ſped ſo iourney ſhee arriued noble citie roome ſhe tooke vp lodging néere pallaice whereas emperor deuiſing lordes feat warre ide went thether knéeled downe ſaluted emperour lord emperour romanes ſawe goodly yong man ſo humbly ſaluted regarded much beautie ſawe emperour ſayd vnto much paine pouertie emperour ſayd fréend thou art good kindred entertaine thée court bountie thinke thée alſo thy good lineage sir quoth ide god giue grace may doe ſuch ſeruice may bee pleaſure daughter oliue quoth emperour loue haue entertained squier ſerue father quoth oliue thanke ſéemeth hee come good stocke seruant great ſeaſon better contented emperour ſayd vnto ide freend ſerue well behold héere daughter loue entirely deliuer ſerue haue moe child ſhee therefore ſerue truely man ought doe come ſuch lineage ſerue well truely neuer life ſo good aduenture sir quoth ide ſhall doe ſo much grace god ſhee ſhall bée well content sir nothing lightly doe ſerue noble man warre ſhall defend ſelfe truſt aſwell another alſo ſerue table king quéene fréend quoth emperour doe thus ſay welcome
