bourdeaux haue ſuch truſt god vertue armes thinkes mine enemy doe flye away sir quoth croiſſant ſhall doe ſo much grace god enemy ſhall haue leaſure graunt v victorie ſecond battaile earle remons sonne led father ſayd hee ſhould day ſhew foorth vertue proweſſe third battaile earle remon duke callaber guiding thereof ſet euery battaile fiftéen thouſand men earle remon went euerie battaile ſtirring moouing doe well earle ſent meſſenger hoaſt sarazins ſhewe comming chriſtian men tent fiue battailes number hundred thouſand sarazins whereof two king foure admiral meſſenger meſſuage done hée returned earle remon ſhewed hee heard ſéene croiſſant ſayd earle sir pray ſhew mee armes two sarazin kinges doe beare intent may know ſooner great men bee ſlaine ſooner flye becauſe abaſh ſooner diſcomfited men without lord ſhéepe without ſhepheard earle ſhewed armes badge sir quoth croiſſant ſince hereof aduertiſed ſhall neuer reſt vntill haue encountred god ſaue mine armes good ſword paynim ſaw well chriſtian men comming caſt vp great crie ſo maruailous none ſo hardy thereof abaſhed ſéemed world arriued croiſſant ſawe sarazins approach aduaunced battaile ioyned couched speare ſtrake therewith king belmarins sonne ſo spearehead paſſed bodie foote ſo drawing speare sarazin fell downe dead among horſe féele whereof paynim great dolour croiſſant hadde ſlaine king belmarins sonne came nephewe king granado croiſſant bare earth ſo rudely falling brake necke ran third fourth ſlew long speare held ceaſed ſlay beat downe sarazins speare broken tooke sword wherewith hee claue sarazins braines cutte armes handes hee made among ſuch ſlaughter ſo hardie sarazin durſt abide full ſtroake fled ſhéepe doe wolfe anon tidings brought king belmarin son ſlaine young knight maruailes battaile king knew sonne ſlaine wept ſorrow made promiſe rather die death sonne ſhould vnreuenged therewith preaſſed battaile met comming duke callabers seneſchall ſtrake speare ſuch wiſe ran cleane ſo fell downe dead battaile began fiercely prouaunce callaber valiantly earle remon came battaile met admirall cordes gaue ſuch ſtroake ſword helmet claue head braines ſo fell downe dead hee ſawe king granado ſlewe many chriſtian man earle remon tooke ſpeare ran kinge ſtrake ſo viſor helmet hee fell earth féet vpward among owne men béen ſlain men ſuccoured another place croiſſant hee ſaw king belmarin road ſéeking croiſſant reuenged death sonne king ſaw croiſſant beating horſe men none could reſiſt againſt great deſire reuenged ſayd croiſſant oh thou falſe traytour hath ſlaine ſon ought greatly laud praiſe mahomet may bee reuenged vpon thée couched ſpeare ſtrake croiſſant middeſt ſhéeld ſo ſpeare flew péeces ſtroake croiſſant remooued though ſtriken ſtone wall croiſſant ſore diſpleaſed king giuen ſuch ſtroake let goe bridle horſe lifted vp ſword hand ſtrake king paſſed ye corner helmet ſuch wiſe ſtrake cleane aſunder ſtroake glaunced clouen head guirdle ſword turned alighted vppon horſe necke ſo ſtrake necke cleane aſunder ſuch ſort force king tumbled earth ſore aſtonied ſtroke receiued béen quickly reſcued croiſſant ſtriken head sarazins remounted againe king ran croiſſant caſt dart iauelins haue ſlain durſt approch néere ſo much feared howbeit hurt diuers place hee held ſword handes wherewith hee ſtrake man full ſtroake hee claue head braines hee ſawe great admirall spaine gaue ſuch ſtroake head clouen chinne ſo hee fell downe dead great ſorrowe made sarazins eſpecially king granado croiſſant ſaw knewe well armes whereof hee ioyfull croiſſant approached gaue ſuch ſtroke helmet head clouen braines ſo kinge fell downe dead croiſſant ran bare sarazins banner wheron painted image mahomet hee ſtrake bare reuerſe ſtroake betwéene necke ſholders head helmet flewe field layd ſo thicke preaſſe anone made way sarazins would faine haue raiſed vp againe banner could sarazins ſaw king dead banner lying ground courage beganne faile brayed opened array began looſe place croiſſant tooke héed nothing ſlay great captaines laſt ſawe kinge belmarin ſlaine many chriſtian man day croiſſant gaue ſuch ſtroake right ſhoulder arme ſhéeld fell earth reaſon great dolour king felt fel aſwound among horſe féete whereas died miſerably duke callaber earle remon regarding hye déedes armes done atchieued croiſſant hadde great maruell force puiſſance bleſſed houre hee borne thanking god comming thether reſted beheld made enemy fly away none ſo hardy abide finally ſhoulde rehearſe hye déedes croiſſant day would ouerlong declare great proweſſe paynim sarazins vtterly diſcomfited happie could ſaue himſelfe thus fled partes towards seaſide moe ſlaine flying plaine battaile thence seaſide wayes couered dead men ſuch might ſaue themſelues ship happie verie eſcaped chace done prouaunce callaber came bootie excéeding great earle remon diſtributed ſo liberally therof euery man wel contented ſuch rich tent sarazins could bee valued whereby ſuch battaile rich euer • freends chap clxxvii ¶ great honour earle remon croiſſant would haue giuen daughter mariage whereof earles son ſore enuious thought ſame night haue murdered noble croiſſant bed fayled noble croiſſant ſlew afterward fled away faſt might battaile finiſhed sarazins dead earle remon great reuerence came vnto croiſſant tooke hand ledde towne betwéen duke callaber himſelfe great honor could deuiſe ſo entred towne great ioy ſolemnitie receiued came pallaice vnarmed refreſhed duke callaber earle remon came croiſſant earle ſayd oh right noble knight repleat vertues hie proweſſe whome man comparable ſtrong arme ſhéeld refuge countrey prouaunce languedoc thy hye proweſſe day thou haſt ſaued one quarter chriſtendome whereby faith chriſt exalted thou •••• eſt béene béene abated ſtaunched mee ſay recount goodneſſe haue done v day lyeth reward thy pleaſure abaſe thy ſelfe ſo lowe take daughter marriage would gladly ſée giue thée one halfe euer haue fairer iewell richer cannot giue déere daughter whome loue entirely ſhée moſt faire ſwéete humbleſt damſell liuing croiſſant well vnderſtood earle remon hee ſayd sir courteſie rich guiftes offer mee refuſe thanke hartely thereof daughter offer giue truſt ſhall doe honour vpon head ſhall ſet crowne gold make empreſſe rome whereas ſhe ſhall ſerued honoured ladie ouer countrey earle heard anſweare croiſſant verie ioyfull sonne preſent néere hand rage diſpleaſure ſayd inragedly god croiſſant ſince thus ſhall bée diſenherited father giue right appertaineth grant thereto ſhal make die ill death though doe treaſon thou ſhalt neuer haue ſiſter marriage thus thought ye earles sonne worke againſt croiſſant knew nothing thereof thus without god help likely haue béene ſlaine pitiouſly began great ioy pallaice earle remon went ſée daughter ſayd déere daughter know troth haue giuen mariage moſt faire hardyeſt knight euer guirt ſword croiſſant ſée héere deliuered brought ſeruice fréedome béen loſt hye proweſſe béene paynim diſcomfited damſell heard father ſhe right ioyfull thanked god ſaid sir ſince pleaſure giue noble knight ſhall refuſe content fulfill pleaſure whereof croiſſant ioyfull ſhee ſo faire euerie man maruaile thereof damſell ſaluted croiſſant ſayd sir comming ſuccours ought ioyfull wée reſtored ioy loſt ladie quoth croiſſant ſo goeth work lord god men make battailes god giueth victorie thus deuiſing entred chamber whereas board readie ſpread izacars earles son would come went ſecret place towne thether hée ſent ten affinitie whome hee perfect affiance ſhewed intention determined croiſſant bed ſléepe murder bedde squier alſo well heard enterprize determined doe ſayd himſelfe ſurely would aduertiſe croiſſant malicious enterprize intent ſhould ſurprized departed priuily could ſo came croiſſant ſhewed earles sonne ten men courage noble man murder neuer treſpaſſe sir quoth squier may doe pleaſe except finde remedie loſt croiſſant heard hee trembled diſpleaſure thought within himſelfe would ſhew matter perſon liuing ſware came doe diſpleaſure sword hee woulde cléeue head braines thus matter reſted vntill night ſo went hal among lord found earle made great chéere supper readie ſatte downe ſeruice make rehearſall began ſore wéepe ſo went towne might coulde trauaile long armour hee beheld voide houſe corner ſtreete hee went thether vnarmed armour except ſword ſo white iacket reſted vntill hee came gate called porter deſired open gate ſaying buſineſſe doe little without towne porter anſweared ſtubbornely ſayd rrquireth haſt hée might well abide ſayd hee would open gate vntill faire day fréend quoth croiſſant pray thée ſhew courteſie porter anſwered fiercely ſayd thou doeſt looſe thy labour gate ſhall opened vntill sunne riſe croiſſant ſaw porter would open gate faire meanes hee ſette hand ſword ſayd thou falſe traitour except thou doeſt open ye gate incontinent ſword ſhall ſlay thee porter ſaw croiſſant held naked ſword hand ſtrike great feare came forth haſt keyes hande ſayd sir ſhall open gate good howbeit ſo afraide bodie trembled feare came gate opened wicket croiſſant yſſued vnarmed hadde cloake ouer iacket ſword little purſe guirdle therein twentie shilling monney thus yée haue heard croiſſant yſſued towne niſe prouaunce tooke way towards roome gone two league fiue traytours fled hidden chamber thought croiſſant departed thought would tarie becauſe hee ſlaine earles sonne went chamber making great brute noiſe ſo euerie man roſe pallaice earle himſelfe aroſe came hall sword hand hée found fiue traytours ſhewed certaine wordes betwéene croiſſant sonne fray betwéene whereby sonne ſlaine hand croiſſant hee wilfully entent haue landes deceaſe becauſe haue giuen daughter mariage wée could come ſled departed chamber ſlewe fiue men beſides sonne armed croiſſant armed ſeemed rather ſpirit mortall man ſaw wee could approach becauſe armed ſlew squier earle heard maruaile though ſorrowful went chamber whereas sonne lay dead came great diſtreſſe hee heart fell downe vppon son ſwound came himſelfe hee cried ſayde ah croiſſant acquaintance verie hard commanded men arme incontinent goe croiſſant ſo pitiouſly ſlaine sonne ſayde may take hee ſhall neuer eſcape handes without death pallace towne euerie man armed earle himſelfe armed mounted horſe yſſued gate many people road abroad coū trey ſearching demaunding man met croiſſant could heare certaine newes except one man ſayd met fiue league frō thence went great pace earle heard hee ſaw well labour loſt fellow returned town right ſorrowfull ſore diſpleaſed death sonne yet againe hee greatly complayned croiſſant aduenture ſaide valiant knight coulde bee found neither courteous wiſe would god betwéene good amitie ſo hee daughter marriage deceaſe hee might haue land diuers men ſayd sir lette goe hée ſhee thought marrie nowe let v leaue ſpeaking returne croiſſant chap clxxix ¶ croiſſant arriued subburbs little towne called florencolle lodged among ruffian villaynes fell ſtrife croiſſant ſlewe fledde great daunger howe hee came cittie rome whereas man would giue one morfell bread went lay old pallaice vpon burden ſtrawe croiſsant ſaw departed towne niſe alone afoo • e hee made complaint lord god requiring humbly haue pitie hee went foorth ſo trauailed three day thrée night without meat drinke little bread water ſuch hunger thirſt could ſcarce ſuſtaine himſelfe féet ſo laſt little sunne ſet hee came little towne called florencolle whereof gate ſhutte came thether subburbs hee ſaw houſe like tauerne hée ſware though ſhould ſlaine would goe houſe eate drinke pay well ſhot béen better haue paſſed great perill life yée ſhall heare thus hee approached houſe heard cooke buſie kitchin ſawe great fire chamber greateſt ruffian player dice towne prepared fleſh fiſh supper croiſſant ſaw preparation made sixe ruffian entred houſe ſaluted hoſt demaunded might lodged hoſt ſayd yea hee ſhould well ſerued wine meat ſuch wold demaund croiſſant went ruffian met ſayd hee welcome pinched wincked one eye ſayd ſoftly maſter great trauailer come well point depart ſhall pay ſhot expences anon put dice hand whereby ſhal leaue gowne cappe monney haue croiſſant vnderſtand becauſe ſpake whiſperingly croiſſant ſayd sir eate paying ſhot ſhall turne diſpleaſure fréend quoth maiſter pleaſeth well eate v waſhed together ſate downe table néere fier well ſerued euery thing croiſſant ſet hee began féede well hunger ſo great thrée dayes eaten nothing bread water therefore hee better appetite alſo hee found good wine freſh dranke thereof pleaſure well eaten drunke well chafed reaſon good wine hoſt roſe vp ſayd sir time make reckoning euerie man pay part maiſter ruffian ſayde sir make account doe better ſhew v wee ſhall pay euerie man alike sir quoth hoſt néere reckon yée muſt pay twelue ſhillings looke euerie man pay part maſter ruffian began ſweare bloud wound ſhould play dice ſée ſhould pay hee ſayd croiſſant fréend muſt come play v behold heere thrée dice good ſquare wee muſt doe ſo one muſt pay whole expences depart sir quoth croiſſant ſhall néede play dice know ſhall pay ſhot pay together without ſtrife ſayd▪ well content therewith thanked one falſeſt villayne among wilfully caſt downe potte wine vpon table whereof fellowes blamed anſweared ſayd sir néed angry therewith none drinke thereof better haue freſh pot wine new veſſell ſayd well true ſo hoſt brought new pot full wine ſayd sir potte wine firſt reckoning potte newe account maiſter ruffian ſayd croiſſant sir take caſt dice firſt caſt ſhalbe croiſſant beheld fiercely ſayd nay sir kéepe mée neuer played dice life content twelue ſhillings ſhall pay ſhot reaſon longe voyage haue made well fourniſhed monney haue thirtéen shilling purſe maiſter ſayd thou art better arrayed thou muſt vſe thy tongue otherwiſe thou ſhalt thus ſcape thou ſhalt leaue thy gowne pay ſhot morrow morning another ruffian ſayd haue hoſe ſhooes morrow buy fiſh dinner croiſſant heard villaynes began change colour ſore diſpleaſed ſayd right fiercely sir leaue clattering yet haue xiij s̄ purſe wil giue rather ſhould diſpleaſed think ought ſuffice sir noble man lately made knight againe countrey would neuer come thence ſéeke ſuch aduentures ought beare honour ſince ſhew knight ruffian ſayd word preaching ſhould auaile muſt leaue gowne iacket hoſe ſhooes croiſſant repleat yre ſurcot furred armin caſt ſayd sir ought content ought quit ruffian vnderſtood cried ſhould put hoſe ſhooes guirdle purſe gowne bad quickely deliuer auoid houſe ſayd lodging hoſt pleaſe villaynes ſayd ſayd troth croiſſant full yre claue head téeth ſo hee fell downe dead chimney another hee ſtrake head ſlewe third fourth two ſo great feare fled away hoſt began crie théefe murderer croiſſant would doe hurt hee yſſued houſe ſword hand ran faſt could vntill without subburbs ranne field ouer hedge diches entent none ſhould follow hearkened towards towne hee heard great cry noiſe hoſt houſe came whereby neighbour taylours shoomakers draper men al craft came houſe ſuch noiſe made ſubburbs towne gate opened burgeſſes yſſued came houſe whereas noiſe magiſtrates towne came thether ſawe men lye dead demaunded hoſt done murder sir quoth hoſt vagabond hath done bigge mightie neuer ſawe mine eye man better made fourmed fledde away ſword hand yonder hye way sir god ſake come néere hee ſéemeth man hee angrie hée like man wittes without feare doubt magiſtrates commaunded follow horſebacke afoote ranne armour though captaine greatly afraide yet hee would bee firſt ſhould go foorth loued better another ſhold take aduantage thus ſides horſebacke afoote followed croiſſant kept high way far night alſo many would chafe themſelues ouer much ſéeke wold make preaſſe receiue offering becauſe feared finde ſought long ſpace field high wayes could finde returned towne croiſſant went euer townward ſword naked hand hee ſawe two league entred high way praiſed god hee ſo eſcaped without daunger hee ſore diſpleaſed neuer penny purſe nothing sword coat rich purſe guirdle alſo ſawe winter froſt ſnow alſo felt cold winde much ill thus hee went foorth night next day vntill néere night arriued village faine ſell ſword lacke monney pay ſhot came lodge ſerued euerie thing would haue morning departed ſold purſe much hee could get hee trauailed ſo long hee approached roome hee came lodging without gate lodged night morning demaunded hoſt whome towne appertained lord thereof name gouerned towne hoſt ſayd fréend hee nowe lord héere named guymart puille hee came hether young lord faireſt young gentleman euer ſéene sonne noble emperour ide ſomewhat reſemble ſo ill rule ſo full folly rich wealth father left hée ſpent gaue away euerie man would craue thing ſo end hee left himſelfe nothing liue heard ſay himſelfe ſuch ſhame departed priuily squier went ſéeke aduentures man knoweth whether euer come againe communaltie cittie made little thereof hee departed ſent king guymart puille whome haue made emperour empire croiſſant vnderſtood hoſt complained right pitiouſly himſelfe ſayde ala poore caitiffe ſhall thus haue loſt al mine inheritance without recouerie beſides haue nothing ſpend haue trade liue muſt behooue die hunger cold haue fiue twentie ſhillings ſould purſe thus well could continued till lent ſeaſon began ſomewhat hotter euerie day morning would heare ſeruice euerie man ſaw beheld greatly ye great beautie diuers knew would make ſemblance thereof intent wold giue nothing ſawe would ſhun way becauſe ſhould know many hee done much good vnto giuen ſuch wiſe become rich poore none would offer
